Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 Who we serve?
Who we are?
W e provide services to over 2,300 children 
and adults across 315 locations. We work 
with the health and social care authorities 
of England and Wales and employ more 
than 7 ,000 people.
Cambian is one of the largest providers  
of specialist behavioural health services  
for children and adults in the UK. 
The Group’ s services have a specific focus 
on individuals who present with high 
severity needs, challenging behaviours 
and who have complex care requirements.

Mental health
Providing rehabilitation 
services for adults with 
mental health conditions  
such as schizophrenia, 
personality disorder or  
severe depression, to  
enable a transition back  
into the community or to  
life in a lower severity setting.
Intellectual disabilities
Supporting people with 
conditions that are generally 
present at birth such  
as autism and learning 
difficulties, to enable  
them to develop abilities  
that lead to a life of  
increased independence  
and community integration. 
Specialist children’s services Specialist adult services
Acquired brain injury
Helping those people with  
a brain injury from, for 
example, an accident or 
trauma to the brain, to recover 
and re-acquire skills lost  
as a result of their injury,  
and subsequently lead as 
independent a life as possible. 
We provide these services  
in hospital or community 
based environments.
Deaf
Providing specialist care  
for children who are deaf  
or have significant hearing 
impairment and associated 
challenging behaviours. 
Fostering
Providing care and emotional 
support to children and  
young people who cannot  
be cared for by their own 
parents or family.
We provide these services  
in specialist residential 
homes, schools, colleges  
and hospitals with specialist 
staff to support each  
setting. We also support 
these children through  
foster parents.

Roll out of specialist  
personality disorder services
In 2015 we opened 48 places in three 
hospitals for adults with a personality 
disorder. We are now a leading provider 
of personality disorder services in the UK. 
 
Greater specialisation and 
move to higher acuity services 
In response to customer demands, we 
are increasing the focus of our services 
on specific conditions (for example in 
Adult Autism and Children’s Learning 
Disabilities), and continue to move to 
higher acuity services (for example 
expanding our offering for children who 
have suffered from neglect or abuse). 
 
By the Bridge, delivering  
on our strategic objective  
to grow our fostering 
capability for higher  
severity children
With our customers preferring a family 
setting where possible for looked after 
children, fostering has been a focus  
for Cambian. With a strong reputation  
for supporting children with high 
severity needs, By the Bridge has 
significantly increased Cambian’s 
capability in this area.
 
Added 321 net places to  
the Group in 2015
We have increased the capacity of the 
Group by over 12% in the year. We now 
have a total capacity of 2,989 places 
which we expect to mature over  
the next 18 months, providing the 
opportunity for growth in revenue  
and profits over the period.
Operational highlights
Performance review
p.32
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 5
Strategic report Chairman’s statement
Overview
Operationally, 2015 looked as if it would  
be a year of achievement. We continued  
to experience significant demand for our 
services, our strong quality ratings were 
maintained, we broadened the range of 
our services with the acquisition of By the 
Bridge, a specialist fostering business, and 
we added significantly to our number of 
places in an ambitious expansion drive. 
Regrettably, our expansion plan was  
in retrospect overly ambitious and  
this is reflected in our disappointing 
financial performance. 
Difficulties in recruiting and training staff, 
particularly in Children’s Services, left us 
unable to open some of our new facilities 
on time, and in order not to sacrifice 
quality, we made a number of unit level 
decisions to block or slow admissions, 
which resulted in revenues falling short  
of expectations. 
This was further exacerbated by failures  
in forecasting and controlling our cost 
base during a period of integration  
and high growth, and has resulted in 
adjusted EBITDA over 12% lower than  
the previous year.
In response to this, we commissioned 
PricewaterhouseCoopers to undertake  
a financial review of certain aspects of  
the Group’s cost management. In addition,  
we are currently implementing a number 
of remedial actions to improve our cost 
control, forecasting and management of 
our suppliers. We have restructured our 
central functions and more closely aligned 
them with the business, resulting in cost 
savings, and we have reduced our growth 
plan so that our focus is now on filling 
existing capacity.
Christopher Kemball
Chairman
Cambian has continued to deliver high 
quality outcomes for the children and 
adults placed in our care.
We hired Martin Hopcroft, who has 
restructuring and turnaround experience,  
in late 2015 and he was appointed as 
Interim CFO in early 2016. In addition  
we have hired additional resource to  
focus on managing our cost base  
with an emphasis on procurement.
We are currently undertaking a search 
process for a permanent CFO. 
Financial results
Revenue increased by 21% to £290.1 million 
(2014: £240.6 million). Adjusted EBITDA was 
£42.5 million (2014: £48.4 million) with 
adjusted EBITDA margin down from 20.1% 
to 14.7%. Operating loss was £7.6m (2014: 
£7.1m profit). Adjusted earnings per share 
were 10.6p (2014: 11.0p). Statutory basic  
loss per share was 5.4p (2014: 6.1p loss). 
The Group’s total capacity
1
 increased from 
2,668 to 2,989 in the year with average 
occupancy of 78% (2014: 81%). 
As previously advised, the Board is not 
recommending a final dividend and will 
look to reinstate the dividend at an 
appropriate time.
Bank agreement
As announced in March 2016, our financial 
performance has resulted in a breach of our 
banking covenants at 31 December 2015 and 
would also be likely to have led to a breach 
when next tested in the current financial year. 
Accordingly, and as announced in March,  
we agreed a temporary waiver with our 
lending banks to cover this eventuality and  
to facilitate our discussions with them to 
amend our facility agreement.
On 26 April 2016 the Board and the  
Group’s lending banks agreed terms for 
the amendment of the Group’s £290m 
Facilities Agreement, the provisions of 
which are set out within the Finance  
review on page 36. 
1  2014 capacity and occupancy have been adjusted to remove CAMHS and Sexual Trauma school places where, although the education capacity is separately registered, the fee is combined 
within the residential facility fee. The impact is a reduction in 2014 closing capacity of 82 places and a reduction in 2014 closing occupancy of 35 occupants. 
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 6 Strategy update
The Board has been reviewing its strategic 
options in light of the agreed terms for the 
amendment of its banking facilities as well 
as the wider market environment in which 
it is operating.
The Board has concluded that it will continue 
to focus on its leading position in Children’s 
Services and has appointed advisors to 
review its strategic options in the Adult 
Services business, which may or may not 
lead to a sale of all or part of this division. 
No final decisions have been made on this 
or any other strategic option and the Board 
will provide updates as appropriate.
Quality of care
Ensuring high levels of care quality for  
the individuals we look after is core to  
our business. I am therefore pleased  
to confirm that as at 31 December 2015, 
92% of our adult facilities and 83% of our 
children’s facilities were rated either “Good” 
or “Outstanding” by our regulators, CQC 
and Ofsted respectively, at a time when 
they are rightly increasing the standards 
they expect from care providers.
We are still aiming to improve the delivery  
of what we believe are life-changing 
outcomes for our patients by supporting 
them with our highly skilled specialist 
teams and deploying a therapy-led 
approach in modern and friendly 
surroundings. Our objective is to increase  
the proportion of our facilities rated “Good”  
or “Outstanding” over the medium term.
We make considerable efforts to anticipate 
and efficiently deliver the services required by 
our customers and regulators. As Chairman, 
I now meet CQC and Ofsted annually to 
discuss areas of mutual interest and concern. 
In this regard, we also invited David Behan, 
the Chief Executive of the CQC, to attend our 
Board and Audit and Risk Committee in 
August so that he could see, understand  
and comment on how we operate.
Board changes
In July 2015, Dr Graham Rich joined the 
Board as a non-executive director and 
member of the Nomination and Audit  
and Risk Committees. Graham qualified  
in medicine and has spent his career in  
the healthcare profession where he gained 
significant experience in running two NHS 
organisations as well as having been 
Director of Health Services at The Boston 
Consulting Group, where he is now a 
Senior Advisor. 
On 2 November 2015 it was announced 
that Andrew Griffith would stand down 
from the Board after the announcement  
of the 2015 full year results. Accordingly, 
Andrew will resign from the Board on  
27 April 2016 and will leave the business 
shortly thereafter. Martin Hopcroft was 
appointed as Interim CFO early in 2016  
and we are currently undertaking a  
search process for a permanent CFO.
We are pleased today to announce the 
appointment of Mike Butterworth as an 
additional non-executive director with 
immediate effect.
Our people
The welfare of our dedicated and  
skilled staff is critical to achieving the  
best possible outcomes for those placed  
in our care. During 2015, we conducted  
a thorough review of our staff pay and 
conditions to ensure that we are in line  
with salaries in the NHS and our private 
sector competitors. As a result, we have 
simplified our pay scales, introduced 
additional pay for achieving relevant 
qualifications and linked these to the 
Government’s announced National  
Living Wage (“NLW”) levels, irrespective  
of an employee’s age. 
The Board would like to take this 
opportunity to thank all our staff for their  
hard work and dedication throughout the 
year. It is much appreciated.
Governance overview
p.42
Pricing
We have engaged with our customers 
since last November to discuss and agree 
increased prices for existing service users 
to reflect the NLW introduction and other 
factors, with the aim of ensuring that there 
will be no negative impact on the business. 
We are pleased with the progress we have 
made so far.
Outlook
The results for 2015 were very disappointing 
but our remedial actions are taking effect. 
We continue to experience strong demand 
for our specialist services and trading to 
date is in line with the Board’s expectations. 
As previously advised, the result for the first 
half will be lower than H1 2015. The Board is 
confident that growth will be resumed for 
the year as a whole.
Despite the challenges we faced, we 
should not lose sight of the fact that 
Cambian remains fundamentally a good 
business with a strong value proposition 
for its customers. 
Our agenda is clear: continue to implement 
the remedial action programme; ensure 
we meet our obligations under the agreed 
terms for the amendment of our bank 
facilities; and continue to deliver the 
highest quality specialist services our 
customers demand.
Christopher Kemball
Chairman
26 April 2016

Overview
Our failure to recruit and train staff to  
the required standards meant that we 
were unable to increase occupancy in line 
with our strategic plan. These operational 
events were compounded by weaknesses 
in our financial procedures and forecasting, 
which impacted our ability to adjust our 
cost base in a timely manner. 
Consequently, the year ended with a 
disappointing financial performance as 
revenues increased but were lower than 
expected and the impact on margins 
impacted profitability. 
During the year we became the largest 
provider of therapeutic fostering services 
through the acquisition of By the Bridge. 
Additionally, we launched a number of 
new specialist services.
Despite the disappointment of our 
financial results, we remain confident in 
the business. Cambian is a leader in the 
provision of high quality care in a market 
where there is urgent need. Our focus in 
the short-term is the ongoing remedial 
action plan to boost occupancy levels  
and to put the Group on a sound financial 
footing to enable sustainable profitable 
growth, including reviewing the Group’s 
strategic options.
Business performance
In 2015 the Group delivered revenue 
growth of 21% (2014: 12%), with an Adjusted 
EBITDA margin of 14.7% (2014: 20.1%).  
The revenue growth includes the impact  
of current and prior year acquisitions as 
well as revenue from new occupants in  
our sites. 
We did however experience a revenue  
and occupancy shortfall against our initial 
expectations, in part due to difficulties in 
recruiting sufficient skilled staff in our new 
sites and to replace normal turnover in 
existing sites, particularly in our Children’s 
Services division in the second half of the 
year. The Group’s average occupancy in 
the year was 78% (2014: 81%).
 
Going into 2015, we had budgeted a 
significant increase in costs over 2014 in 
two main areas: first, an investment in our 
central functions such as HR, Marketing 
and Quality to build an operating platform 
capable of delivering significant growth; 
and, secondly, costs relating to newly 
opened units which are incurred ahead  
of revenue from occupancy. 
With the shortfall in revenue against our 
budget, these costs impacted our profit in 
the year and, in addition, we experienced 
cost overruns in areas such as recruitment 
costs and repairs and maintenance. Our 
forecasting of costs was poor in part due  
to issues arising from the integration of  
the Cambian and Advanced Childcare 
back offices in the year. Once the revenue 
shortfall was identified, it took longer than 
expected to manage down non-wage 
costs during the year. 
Saleem Asaria 
Chief Executive Officer
The demand for Behavioural Health services 
in the UK is strong and we remain confident 
in our business, providing high quality care 
where there is urgent need.
Cambian Group plc

Chief Executive’s strategic review In response to this performance, we have 
taken a number of steps: 
• We commissioned 
PricewaterhouseCoopers to undertake 
a financial review of certain aspects  
of the Group’s cost management.
• We are currently implementing  
a number of remedial actions to 
improve our cost control, forecasting 
and management of our suppliers.
• We have put on hold new openings  
to focus on filling the Group’s current 
capacity from existing sites and those 
sites already in development. This will 
reduce 2016 openings to approximately 
40 net additional places allowing for 
improved margins as the portfolio of 
facilities matures. 
• We have restructured our central 
functions: we devolved our HR 
department into regional centres, 
reporting to the operating divisions  
and thereby improving the connection 
between staffing needs and our 
recruitment pipeline; we have 
disbanded our M&A and asset 
acquisition teams; and restructured  
our quality team. All of these steps  
will generate ongoing savings for  
the Group. 
• Finally, we hired Martin Hopcroft,  
who has restructuring and turnaround 
experience, in late 2015 and he was 
appointed as Interim CFO in early  
2016. In addition we have hired 
additional resource to focus on 
managing our cost base with an 
emphasis on procurement.
In 2015 we have focused on four main areas:
Delivering value for  
our customers
Investing to expand  
our specialist services
Investing in our  
internal capabilities
Improving the life 
outcomes for the 
people in our care

Strategic report • Thirdly, we aligned our management, 
training and therapeutic capabilities to 
these services. 
In line with these areas of focus, Cambian 
has grown its capacity significantly in the 
year, adding a total of 377 places. With  
56 places being closed or re-provisioned, 
we added a net 321 places in the year 
including 259 in our Children’s Services  
and 62 in our Adult Services. 
With a focus on maturing our existing 
business, our growth plan for 2016 is 
restricted to completing units that are 
currently in construction, so we anticipate 
adding approximately 40 net new places  
to capacity in the year.
Children’s Services
The focus of our growth plan in the year  
was in the Children’s division.
We increased our education services 
significantly, in particular adding three 
large schools: Bletchley, Spring Hill and 
Potterspury Lodge (with a combined 
capacity of 166 places). These offer 
Service delivery
The demand for Behavioural Health 
services in the UK remains strong, driven  
by underlying trends of a higher incidence 
and better diagnosis of conditions, 
together with greater quality of life 
expectations for those people impacted.  
In addition, HM Government continues  
to outsource such services, with high 
expectations for the quality of service 
provided and the outcomes expected. 
In order to ensure that we are well-
positioned to take advantage of these 
market dynamics we made significant 
changes in 2015:
• First, we moved to a greater 
specialisation and delineation of our 
services (for example in Autism and 
Personality Disorders). 
• Secondly, we continued our move to 
higher severity services (for example for 
children who have suffered from sexual 
exploitation or abuse, or children and 
adolescents suffering from mental  
health conditions).
significant opportunity for future revenue 
growth as we build occupancy and focus 
their offerings on higher value services  
to address more acute needs. We have 
also grown our Children’s residential 
services, in particular for children 
suffering from abuse or neglect or  
with mental health conditions. 
We have previously highlighted fostering  
as an area that we wished to grow. To this 
end, we were pleased to acquire By the 
Bridge in March 2015. By the Bridge operates 
at the high-severity end of fostering and has 
built a reputation for providing high quality, 
therapeutic fostering services and for 
successfully placing children with complex 
needs in a family environment. As such,  
it occupies a niche position between 
traditional fostering and residential care and 
now forms an integral part of our Children’s 
Services offering. Cambian’s existing 
fostering operation has been integrated  
into By the Bridge during the year. Our focus 
is now on foster carer recruitment to drive 
placement numbers. At 31 December 2015 
the Group had 668 fostering placements 
(2014: 203 placements), of which 501  
related to By the Bridge. 
Adult Services
The Adult Services market is more mature 
than the Children’s market. However,  
we see opportunities in specialist sub-
segments in the Adult market and, to  
that end, we opened four larger units  
in Adult in the year with including two 
Personality Disorder units, an Acquired 
Brain Injury unit and a unit for Adults  
with autism. 
We have two Woodleigh units under 
construction and due to open later this 
year and, with a good performance from 
existing Woodleigh units since acquisition 
in 2014, we are confident that there will be 
strong demand for these services.
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 10
Chief Executive’s strategic review
continued Quality and regulatory 
Our ambition is to be the highest quality 
provider of behavioural health services  
to Children and Adults. It is pleasing to 
report, therefore, that our regulatory  
scores remained strong throughout the  
year with 85% of our facilities rated good  
or outstanding with Ofsted or the CQC  
as at 31 December 2015. We underwent  
no embargoes and we currently have  
no facilities with compliance notices. 
The sector is seeing an increasingly 
stringent regulatory environment with  
an enhanced rigour of inspections which  
we both welcome and are well-positioned 
to benefit from in this drive to improve the 
focus on quality of care. 
At the same time we have seen an 
extension of the time taken to register new 
sites and services and this has contributed  
to delays in opening new sites.
From a governance perspective, in order  
to ensure an integrated approach to risk  
we have now merged the Audit Committee 
and the Quality and Risk Committee.  
The re-named Audit & Risk Committee  
now directly oversees all elements of risk  
in the business.
Fees 
In April 2015 we increased fees, across the 
majority of our services, by an average of 
2% for new admissions. From the beginning 
of 2016, we have further increased fees for 
new service users. 
As previously indicated, we are supportive 
of the introduction of the NLW and we  
are in negotiation with commissioners to 
mitigate the net impact by corresponding 
fee increases for all existing service users. 
We have engaged with our customers  
since last November to discuss and  
agree increased prices to reflect the  
NLW introduction and other cost factors  
with the aim of ensuring that there  
will be no negative impact on margins.  
We are pleased with the progress we  
have made so far. 
Summary and outlook 
It is a disappointment to report poor 
results, especially when they disguise  
the very real progress we did make  
during the year in terms of new service 
delivery and care quality.
We have moved quickly to remedy the 
issues facing our business and have 
already seen positive trends, including 
improved occupancy levels, in the first 
quarter of 2016. 
We are focussing on our core business.  
We are filling our existing capacity, 
ensuring that we have the necessary 
systems in place and deploying staff  
more efficiently.
We remain confident for the medium- 
term outlook and also the Group’s 
longer-term potential.
Saleem Asaria 
Chief Executive Officer 
26 April 2016

Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 12 Amy’s story
Amy was admitted to Cambian Acer Clinic from  
a secure service. She had a chaotic lifestyle, with 
serious self-harming behaviours and a lack of  
any meaningful interaction with health services. 
The Cambian team focused on engagement  
with Amy so they could unpick the cause of her 
self-harming behaviour. Over time these events 
became fewer as other coping mechanisms 
helped her through difficult times. Amy is looking 
forward to discharge shortly and setting up her 
own home in the community.
Cambian delivery 
Cambian Acer Clinic 
Cambian Acer Clinic in Derbyshire was opened  
in May 2015, and is a state of the art service  
with 28 beds for women with complex mental 
health needs, particularly those with a personality 
disorder. Rehabilitation is provided in a therapeutic 
environment, with a level of security matched  
to individual needs. The aim of the treatment, 
rehabilitation and re-socialisation programme  
is to prepare the people in our care either for 
transfer to placements with less support, or for  
a life in the community. 
…to deliver

Max’s story
Max was taken into care aged 9 
having been removed from his 
parents by the police due to neglect 
and abuse. After four placement 
breakdowns he was placed with  
By the Bridge. He arrived with anxiety, 
low in confidence. In a safe ‘home’ 
environment Max is starting to  
thrive. With improving confidence  
and self-esteem he attends his  
local school and for the first time  
in his life has the stability to build his  
future along with enjoying the typical 
experiences of any child, such as 
going on holiday with his carers.
Cambian delivery 
By the Bridge – a fostering  
service that increases  
our pathway offering for 
our customers.
Operating with children with high 
severity needs, fostering services from 
By the Bridge have built a reputation 
for providing high quality, therapeutic 
fostering and for supporting children 
with complex needs in a family 
environment. Cambian can now offer 
a complete pathway for our Children’s 
Service from residential care to the 
ultimate aspiration of children living 
with a foster family, through to 
returning home to their birth family 
where possible.
 – Data presented at the Royal College of 
Psychiatrists rehabilitation conference  
in November 2015 showed that over  
70% of patients discharged from the 
Cambian Churchill hospital in London 
remain within services with less 
support and in a less restrictive 
environment one year later. 
 – Cambian’s facilities have high 
regulatory scores, and the Group 
operates a robust risk management 
framework that encompasses both 
operational and clinical risks. 
 – With a well-developed sales and 
marketing function, we maintain 
strong relationships with our 
customers and understand customer 
preferences very well. We do not 
require long-term contracts, but 
rather work with our customers  
to ensure that we offer services  
in areas with strong demand and 
where our model of high quality 
outcomes can be applied.
Cambian delivers value for 
money to our customers  
in a number of ways:
 – Through the efficacy of our operating 
model and by providing specialist 
services, we offer value for money  
to our customers and a service with  
a personalised care pathway. Our 
daily rates often offer savings to  
our customers as compared to the 
equivalent public sector provision.
 – At the same time, we deliver excellent 
outcomes for the people in our care 
with a view to enabling a transition 
back into the community or into a 
lower severity setting. This often 
follows a multi-year history of being 
treated in other high severity services 
at a substantial cost to the funding 
organisation. These outcomes 
provide a strong “cost of life” benefit  
to our customers.

Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 George’s story
George came to Meeko House after a stay in a 
higher acuity service. The aim of his admission  
was to ensure that he had the full support he 
required to cope with his schizophrenia and  
catch up on his schooling by attending Meeko’s 
linked specialist school. After nine months of  
steady progress George was discharged home  
and his support transferred to his community  
CAMHS team. George is sitting his GCSEs  
this summer.
Cambian delivery 
Meeko House – providing vital CAMHS  
(Child and Adolescent Mental Health  
Service) capacity.
Opened in 2015, Cambian Meeko House is a  
16 bed children’s residential home with a full 
multi-disciplinary team catering for twelve to 
eighteen year olds with mental health needs  
and challenging behaviours that prevent them  
from functioning within the community without 
continued support. Our aim is to support the  
young people through an in-depth and integrated 
approach to recovery, in a nurturing and safe 
environment to achieve excellent outcomes. 
Cambian has invested to increase its range  
of CAMHS services so they include a hospital,  
step down services, transitional services from  
child to adult, and an associated school. 
…to provide

the right 
environment.

Annual Report and Accounts 2015 Improving the life 
outcomes for the 
peop le in our care…
…provides 
Britney with

Britney’s story
Britney was diagnosed with severe autism. She 
displayed very challenging behaviours and levels  
of anxiety and would sometimes run away from 
home. Cambian Broughton Lodge used a high level  
of support to address her challenging behaviours, 
and a speech and language therapy programme  
to improve communication. To date Britney has 
significantly reduced the number of behaviour 
incidents, and is learning the key skills to look  
after herself and cope with other people. Her next 
key step will be to move to a supported living service.
Cambian delivery 
Cambian Broughton Lodge – maximising 
independence and improving quality of life.
Opened in 2015, Broughton Lodge is a specialist 
residential home for young adults with autism, learning 
disabilities and complex needs. We aim to provide a 
safe, comfortable and effective care environment for 
those in our care. Our approach is to provide 
personalised learning for residents through experience 
and therapeutic services, empowering individuals to 
progress towards a life with increased independence 
and improved integration into the community. 
Cambian Broughton Lodge also has close links with 
colleges and other educational establishments, 
libraries, voluntary work centres and many other 
community services.

Significant personalised 
outcomes
We actively support every person 
in our care to achieve their 
personal best, these ‘outcomes’ 
are different for everyone. A child 
being placed with a foster family,  
a young person with mental 
ill-health returning home to their 
family, an adult with learning 
disabilities living independently or  
a child with Asperger’s attending 
tertiary education, all are 
significant meaningful outcomes. 
These have a positive impact not 
only on the individual and their 
family, but also the authority that 
funded the placement. 
Outcomes start with clear 
objectives being agreed when  
a person is first placed in one of 
our services. They are supported 
by our therapy programmes and 
care approach. Alongside our 
range of specialist environments 
we can allow these outcomes to 
be realised.
Putting in place clear objectives 
for the people in our care, aligned 
to a care pathway to deliver 
successful outcomes.
Providing people with support at each life stage…
Cambian supports the active progression of the people in our care  
with a range of specialist services that allow for greater independence 
through reduced levels of support. In the example of a child with severe 
autism, this support can be seen through a pathway that could include 
attending a Specialist Education School, transitioning to a Specialist 
College to continue to build lifelong skills and then moving into a 
Specialist Adult service where these skills can be maintained and  
they can achieve their personal best in adult life. 
Strategic report
19
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 Market overview
Cambian operates in the behavioural 
health market in the UK. We work with 
children and adults across a number of key 
specialist care sub-sectors focused within 
a defined, high severity range. The Group 
states this as being 7-9 on a severity scale 
ranging from 0-10. A score of 10 indicates  
a person’s needs would typically be met  
in a fully secure setting, whilst lower  
down the scale 1-3 is where an individual 
functions well in society without the need 
for significant specialist interventions.  
The Group’s services can be divided  
across four areas: Intellectual Disabilities, 
Emotional and Social Difficulties, Mental 
Health and Acquired Conditions.
Funding
Our services are predominantly funded 
through Commissioning Care Groups 
(“CCGs”) who are responsible for 
commissioning primary and secondary 
healthcare services for their local 
communities, and through Local 
Authorities from within their social  
care budgets. In addition, certain  
services are funded through NHS  
England, the central independent 
commissioning body within the NHS.
Emotional and Social Difficulties (“ESD”) cover 
a range of complex and chronic conditions 
experienced by children and young people. 
Conditions include emotional, conduct and 
hyperkinetic disorders, as well as anxiety, 
self-harm, depression, attachment and 
attention deficit disorders. Underlying 
reasons for ESD can include individual and 
external factors with children driven primarily 
by challenging social circumstances or a 
traumatic experience such as neglect  
or abuse. 
The three largest areas in the ESD market 
are the provision of residential care, 
education and fostering services. The UK 
has 66,000 “Looked After Children” who fit 
within this segment. Children placed in 
children’s homes tend to have needs at the 
higher severity end. Cambian is the largest 
provider of specialist children’s homes in the 
UK, with strong and growing positions. In 
the fostering and ESD education markets, 
the acquisition of By the Bridge in March 
2015 has strengthened our position in the 
fostering market, which provides a pathway 
for children placed in children’s homes 
towards care in a family environment. 
Mental Health is the state of emotional and 
psychological being in which an individual  
is unable to use his or her cognitive and 
emotional capabilities, function in society, 
and meet the ordinary demands of 
everyday life. Cambian’s independent 
mental health services provide wrap 
around therapeutic support and treatment 
for people with mental ill health, typically 
for people who are detained under the 
Mental Health Act. There is a recognised 
increase in demand for Child and 
Adolescent Mental Health Services 
(“CAMHS”) in the UK. This increased 
demand, which has also been driven  
by the government’s policy that no young 
people under 18 should be placed in  
adult mental health wards, has placed 
significant strain on services nationally  
and Cambian has responded by  
increasing our investment in this area. 
Independent providers receive funding in 
one of four ways: 
(i)  Spot contracts, or individual placement 
agreements, which generally have  
no minimum term and which offer  
our customers operational flexibility.  
Fees are typically agreed on a case  
by case basis.
(ii)  Framework agreements, which set  
out the key terms on which service 
users will be placed for a set period. 
Within a framework agreement,  
the purchaser does not have any 
minimum purchasing obligations,  
and the actual care package and  
price will be determined at the  
time the placement is made.
(iii)  Block contracts, where terms are 
agreed for a specific volume of 
services to be provided, pre-booked 
over a period of time at a specific 
price. Such block contracts have 
become increasingly uncommon  
over recent years.
(iv)  Private pay or insurance, which  
makes up a very small part of the 
specialist behavioural healthcare 
market. Examples in this category 
would be individuals from outside  
the UK coming here for treatment.
Market segments
An analysis of each of the segments that 
Cambian serves is as follows: 
Intellectual Disabilities relate to those 
conditions that are present at birth, as a 
result of either heredity or environmental 
influences: these are commonly recognised 
as being people with autism or who have 
a learning disability. Such individuals can 
have complex needs, and often challenging 
behaviours. Cambian is one of the UK’s 
leading providers of services for intellectual 
disabilities to both children and adults, 
through our educational and residential 
services for children and young adults, as 
well as rehabilitation hospitals, step-down, 
residential services and day services  
for adults. 
Market dynamics
•  M a r k e t c on s ol i d at i on 
continuing with advantages 
for larger providers 
•  C o m m i s s io n i ng t r e nd s 
driving need for an  
extended care pathway  
for certain services
•  Focus on outcomes driving 
increased specialisation
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 20 Market size and outlook 
In the UK there are estimated to be 
approximately 140,000 individuals  
who require a high intensity service  
within the areas that Cambian serves,  
with the annual spend on these individuals 
being approximately £13bn (Source: 
Company estimates). Approximately  
half of this population’s needs are met  
by independent providers, the remainder 
being public sector provision. 
Our addressable market is seeing 
increasing demand due to a number  
of drivers. As well as population growth,  
the underlying rates of incidence of these 
conditions are increasing, with a greater 
awareness and improving diagnosis of 
conditions. This is illustrated by a rise in UK 
autism prevalence from 39 cases per 10,000 
people in 1979 to approximately 100 cases 
per 10,000 in 2006 (Source: National Autistic 
Society). The independent sector’s role in the 
market has also increased in recent years 
given the benefits specialist providers can 
offer. Whilst the role of private provision 
within the NHS and local authorities remains 
a source of political debate, we believe that 
the trend towards outsourcing behavioural 
health services to specialist independent 
providers will continue to increase, given  
the benefits we can provide.
Acquired Conditions are a disruption in  
brain functioning that is not congenital  
or caused by birth trauma. However, it is  
a severe and life-long disabling condition 
which significantly impairs a person’s  
ability to function in society. The condition  
is manifested by significant decline in 
cognitive functioning and ability or 
deterioration in personality, impulse 
control, judgement, modulation of mood  
or awareness of deficits, typically as a 
result of a motor vehicle accident, stroke or 
substance misuse. Cambian is a relatively 
small provider in this area, but we have  
an additional specialist service due to  
open in 2016 and we believe that the 
segment provides an opportunity for 
growth in the future. 
Regulation 
The market that Cambian serves is 
regulated primarily by the Care Quality 
Commission (“CQC”) and the Office for 
Standards in Education, Children’s Services 
and Skills (“Ofsted”). These bodies control 
and administer the registration, inspection 
and complaints procedures set out under 
applicable laws and regulations. In order 
to open a service, it needs to be registered 
with Ofsted or the CQC, and must pass 
regular inspections to ensure it meets the 
minimum standards and requirements 
prescribed under laws and regulations.

Outputs Growth opportunities through
Cambian provides high quality behavioural 
health services to children and adults in the UK. 
Our business model offers significant growth 
opportunities for the business, both increasing 
our reach to touch more people’s lives, and 
delivering demonstrable value for money to  
our customers.
Everything we do is underpinned by the following 
key principles:
•  Focus on providing a high quality service in our 
specialist markets
•  Rigorous governance and risk management 
•  Delivering an evidence based therapeutic model 
•  Recruiting and retaining high quality staff
Our customers
We provide services for over 300 different 
customers, primarily Local Authorities and 
National Health Service bodies. Each of  
our customers is looking for high quality 
outcomes and value for money, both in terms 
of “day one” cost savings and “whole life” 
benefits for the individual that they place. 
Therapeutically-led 
approach
With a large team of in-house qualified 
therapeutic staff, we follow evidence  
based models that focus on clear 
outcomes. Our clinical staff are all fully 
employed by Cambian and we have 
leading therapeutic models and practices 
which drive outcomes for our service users.
High quality assets 
A key element of our service is providing  
the right environment for the people in  
our care. Since our foundation in 2004 we 
have invested significantly in our property, 
and we have a high quality freehold 
property portfolio of hospitals, schools  
and residential homes.
Dedicated staff
We have over 7,000 employees who,  
on a daily basis, provide high quality care. 
We have training programmes to ensure 
they are equipped with the right skills to 
deliver outcomes that have life changing 
effects for each person.

plan in the year. We are now focussed on

adding to capacity.

Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 25
Strategic report Improving our risk management  
systems and approach
The Group’s business 
involves the care of 
vulnerable people  
with complex needs, 
involving it in significant 
risks. The effective 
management of risk  
has to be a core 
competence and 
operational focus  
of Cambian. 
The 2014 edition of the UK Corporate 
Governance Code (the “Code”) has  
placed greater emphasis on risk and  
the responsibility of boards for an 
organisation’s overall approach to risk.
During the year, the Committee has 
designed and implemented a risk 
management system to allow the Board to 
assess the main risks facing the business 
and will continue to develop and embed 
these processes in the current year.
In the light of this overall responsibility,  
the Board has developed a process for the 
management of risk at Cambian involving:
• Identifying the principal risks that 
threaten the achievement of our 
strategic objectives and assessing  
their significance to the business;
• Putting in place appropriate mitigating 
controls to manage identified risks to  
an acceptable level;
• Escalation and reporting of principal  
risk and control information to support 
management decision making and 
oversight;
• Assigning responsibility and defining 
accountabilities for risk management 
and putting these into practice across  
the Group;
• Having in place an appropriate risk 
management framework aligned to  
and supportive of the delivery of our 
strategy; and
• Continuously monitoring the changing 
risk environment, the Group’s principal 
risks, and the application of the 
framework.
The Board’s process for identifying the 
principal risks, involved risk workshops with 
the senior management team and also with 
their direct reports to identify risks and the 
existing controls in place to manage these 
risks. This process resulted in the description 
of eleven strategic risks facing the Group 
and both the Children’s Services division  
and the Adult Services division have 
developed their own risk registers using  
the same approach. Strategic risks can be 
defined as the uncertainties and untapped 
opportunities inherent in Cambian’s 
strategic plans and how well they are 
executed in the long term. As such, strategic 
risks are key matters for the Board as they 
impinge on the whole Group and its ability 
to deliver its objectives, rather than just 
having an isolated impact on a site,  
region or function.
During the year, Anne Marie Carrie, who 
had chaired the Quality & Risk Committee, 
stood down from the Board to take up  
an executive position within the business. 
Prompted in part by this change, the  
Board undertook a review in the second 
quarter of 2015 of the operation of the  
Audit Committee and the Quality & Risk 
Committee. Following this review, it was 
decided to combine the responsibilities  
of the two committees, so as to create the 
Audit & Risk Committee (the “Committee”) 
as a single point of reference for the 
monitoring of risk, both clinical and 
commercial, and to establish a framework 
for reporting to the Board. The Committee 
is required to consider the nature and 
extent of the risks facing the Group and 
keep them under review. In addition, the 
Committee reviews the risk management 
framework to mitigate such risk, monitors 
the effectiveness of the risk management 
framework and notifies the Board of 
changes in the status and control of risks.
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 26
Risk management Ongoing process for risk identification, 
reporting and management
The Board is ultimately responsible for 
maintaining sound risk management, 
internal control and quality systems across 
the Group and monitoring these systems, 
although responsibility for risk and control 
oversight is principally delegated to the 
Committee, as described above. The Board 
must ensure that there are robust risk 
management and internal control systems 
and, at least annually, carry out a review  
of their effectiveness and report on that 
review to shareholders and the executive 
management team. The executive 
management team is responsible for 
defining, debating and challenging  
the nature of the principal risks and for 
sponsoring risk management activity 
across the Group. They are also 
responsible for ensuring that each of  
the operational services and Group 
functions implement the framework  
and providing challenge on risk issues  
and their mitigation. In parallel with the 
development of the strategic risk register, 
the Company has developed an enhanced 
Lines of defence Function Activity
First line Group’s individual unit managers
•  Apply the Group’s policies and procedures, such as safeguarding and  
health & safety
• Report incidents up to regional or divisional management
Second line
Executive management team
•  Considers any serious incidents, new whistleblowing reports and potential  
risks on a weekly basis and agrees any actions in response
• Reviews the risk register on a monthly basis and agrees any changes in practice  
or procedures
Regular monthly and quarterly 
meetings of executives and  
Risk and Quality function in  
Adult and Children’s Services
• Considers issues raised at hospital clinical governance meetings (Adult Services)  
or from safeguarding meetings (Children’s Services)
•  Reviews findings from site visits by Quality Intelligence team and regulatory 
inspections, such as inspection of children’s facilities under Regulation 44 
Third line
Internal audit
• Tests existing controls on a programme agreed with the Audit & Risk Committee
Clinical governance committee
(chaired by Group clinical director)
• Considers issues raised at clinical governance meetings
•  Reviews findings from site visits by Quality Intelligence team and  
Regulation 44 team
risk reporting framework intended to draw 
together day to day business risks and 
those risks specifically associated with 
clinical and care quality issues. A clear 
framework and cycle of reporting on risk  
is essential in building, implementing and 
developing strategic and operational risk 
management practices across Cambian. 
While the Group’s focus on the quality of 
the services it delivers acts as its principal 
tool for the management of operational 
risks, the risk management framework 
supports the delivery of the Group’s risk 
management objectives and outlines 
policy, application principles, risk oversight 
structures, key accountabilities and 
requirements for identifying, assessing 
reporting and monitoring risk. However, 
effective risk management is not just  
about meeting regulatory requirements. 
Understanding the risks Cambian faces 
and managing them appropriately will 
enhance its ability to make more informed 
decisions, deliver on objectives and 
subsequently improve its performance.  
In addition, managing risk effectively will 
protect and enhance the benefits and 
commitments the Company has made  
to our service users and shareholders,  
and it is this overarching principle that  
is the backbone of our approach to risk 
and control management. 
Responsibility for risk and quality rests  
with each and everyone in the business  
and is monitored by each facility manager  
on a daily basis. Both the Adult Services  
and Children’s Services divisions are 
supported by a dedicated Quality 
Intelligence team (“QI team”), which  
include former regulatory inspectors,  
who assist with regular site visits,  
auditing quality assurance, compliance  
and performance improvement.
The Group’s risk management framework is based on three lines of defence, as outlined below.
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 27
Strategic report At an operational level in Adult Services 
each hospital holds a monthly clinical 
governance meeting to review matters 
such as medication, staffing levels,  
care plans and the like. The output  
from these meetings is reviewed on a 
quarterly basis by the regional clinical 
governance meetings and the Adult 
Services clinical board, which is attended  
by senior operational managers, the 
Quality Intelligence team, and health  
& safety manager. 
The Children’s Services and the educational 
services leadership teams meet weekly to 
review safeguarding and operational risk 
matters and matters arising are considered  
monthly at the Children’s Services residential 
safeguarding board and the education 
monthly management meeting. Any issues 
of immediate concern are raised either at 
the weekly Group executive management 
meeting or escalated further to the Audit & 
Risk Committee.
The management forums in both children’s 
residential and education services report 
ultimately to the Children’s Services 
leadership team, who meet monthly  
and review all safeguarding and other  
risks from the Children’s Services risk 
register, consider any regulatory issues  
or inspections and report to the Clinical 
Corporate Governance meeting.
The executive management team at their 
monthly management meetings consider 
whether, in the light of incidents reported 
from unit managers, the risks identified  
in the Group strategic risk register have 
moved. The meeting also considers the 
effectiveness of existing controls against the 
strategic risks and any mitigating actions 
identified in response to specific incidents. 
The output of the monthly management 
meeting is a risk heat map that identifies  
the likelihood of the risk occurring and the 
financial and reputational impact of the risk 
on the Group, as well as the steps that are 
being taken to reduce any risks identified  
as having increased in either impact or 
likelihood. This map and an explanation of 
the reasons why any risks are identified as 
being high or very high, together with plans 
in place or being formulated to reduce the 
risk, is tabled at each Board meeting for 
consideration by the directors.
In this way we believe that we are able  
to bring together consideration of medical, 
clinical, safeguarding and regulatory risks 
with other commercial risks.
Principal risks & uncertainties
The risks and uncertainties described in 
pages 30 and 31 are considered, at this 
point in time, to have the greatest effect  
on Cambian’s strategic objectives. This list  
is not intended to be comprehensive or 
exhaustive. While the Company can monitor 
risks and prepare for adverse scenarios,  
the ability to affect the core drivers of some 
risks are not within the Group’s control,  
for example changes in government 
regulation or policy.
During 2015 the principal risks identified 
through this process were in respect of the 
Group’s systems and process, in particular 
risks associated with the integration of  
the former Advanced Childcare Limited’s 
finance, HR and payroll systems into the 
existing Cambian systems, and the risk 
associated with the Group’s ambitious 
organic expansion plans. In response  
to these identified risks, the Group 
implemented a review of processes and 
procedures and is currently in the course  
of implementing a number of improved 
processes, and has scaled back the plans 
for organic growth. The other principal risk 
identified through the framework related to 
our Children’s Services which experienced 
some operational fragility caused by a 
difficulty in attracting the right calibre of 
support staff to work in an often challenging 
environment. This risk was manifested in 
delays during the year to openings of new 
facilities and restrictions in the number of 
pupils who could be accommodated at 
some of our schools. To mitigate these risks, 
management over-hauled the Group’s 
recruitment processes, improved induction 
and training and reviewed its pay-scales  
in certain geographical areas.
At the current point in time, the principal 
risks faced by the Group are its high level  
of indebtedness and the risk posed by 
weaknesses in the Group’s management 
information systems and financial controls. 
As indicated in the Chairman’s statement, 
the Board is considering a number of 
strategic options in order to reduce the 
Group’s leverage and is confident that it  
will be able to effect a transaction in order 
to achieve this strategic goal. In addition, the 
Board is working hard to address the risks 
posed by the weakness in the Group’s 
systems and controls with a number of 
improved processes being introduced. 
In addition, from April 2016 the government 
has introduced the national living wage 
which will increase the Group’s employment 
costs. Management have commenced a 
series of negotiations with customers with  
a view to increasing fees for existing service 
users to allow the Group to recover this 
increased cost and not impact on the  
quality of care provided. While the Group 
is reasonably confident, there can be no 
guarantee that it will be possible to fully 
recover the costs associated with the 
introduction of the national living wage 
through increased charges and the Group 
will continue to explore ways of ensuring 
that the impact of this legislative change  
is mitigated.

Strategic report Key risk Description Impact Mitigation Change Assessment
Quality of Service
Failure to provide a high quality and consistent 
level of care for the children and adults placed 
under our charge
• Reputational damage
• Negative government/media attention
• Loss of operating licences
• Reduced regulator assessment scores 
• Commissioners choose other healthcare providers
• Weekly adult and children safeguarding meetings to flag issues and/or lessons learnt
• Annual service performance review (structured interview and a site visit)
• Clinical Governance Committee on-going debate and challenge of clinical performance
• Detailed process in place for foster family recruitment
• Clearly defined operating framework setting out objectives in adult mental health  
and for each specialist area (LD, Autism, Personality Disorders) 
• Clinical Supervision process implemented and supported by on-going monitoring  
and review (staff monthly, managers every three months, clinicians quarterly)
The regulatory environment has 
become more challenging over  
the last financial year
High, principally 
in Children’s 
Services
Regulatory Breach
Loss or suspension of operating licences due  
to a major statutory, regulatory or contractual 
compliance breach 
• Regulatory financial penalties 
• Uninsured claims 
• Brand and reputation damage
• Disciplinary proceedings/removal of staff 
• Site closures
• Staff induction process requires staff to have understanding of regulatory requirements
• Lesson learnt (incidents and CQC feedback) discussed and shared at management meetings
• Established Quality Intelligence and Regulation 44 teams visit sites to audit quality, undertake 
mock inspections and support units in developing improvement plans
Medium
Service Innovation
Insufficient innovation in the business model, 
service offerings and model of care reduces  
our competitiveness in the market
• Commissioners choose other healthcare providers
• Service users receive an out-dated care service
• Metrics developed for measurement of patient outcomes
• Ad-hoc interaction with Department of Health and Government Agencies
Medium
Incident Response
Inability to effectively react and respond to a 
major and or systematic incidents in a timely 
and controlled manner
• Serious injury to service users and staff
• Closure of sites
• Poor registration scores
• Reputational damage
• Each site has a detailed business continuity plan which is reviewed annually and signed  
off by management 
• QFM system used for recording all property maintenance issues that need resolving
• A prioritised maintenance schedule used for programming works
• RIDDOR incident reporting in place at all sites
• Incident reporting provided to the QI team
Medium
Relationships
Failure to create and maintain strong 
relationships with commissioners to ensure 
referrals and conversion
• Loss of service users to other healthcare providers
• Reduction in referrals
• Decline in revenue
• Databases capture data on customers, service users, billings and some contact information
• Commissioning managers are allocated geographic areas of responsibility so understand  
local commissioners well
• Quarterly report produced showing number of placements against target for sales team
• Improved communications between operations and commissioning managers with regard  
to placements at risk and referrals processes
Low
Systems & Processes
Immaturity of financial & operational systems 
and processes prevent effective business 
operations and sustainable future growth
• High amount of manual processes and workarounds required 
increasing scope for human error and cost
• Poor data quality
• Difficulty in forecasting accurately
• High working capital requirement
• Have developed a mapping of systems to provide visibility and fully understand the overall  
systems landscape
• Introduction of improved processes for billing, accounts payable and payroll as part of  
a finance remediation plan
Weakness in systems & processes 
hamper visibility for managing and 
forecasting accurately
High
Attraction & Retention
We fail to attract and maintain an effective,  
high quality resource and talent base
• Inability to deliver a high quality service to the service users due  
to a failure to recruit sufficient high calibre staff
• Inability to meet regulatory requirements
• Beds blocked due to staffing issues leading to a decline in revenues
• New recruitment processes, messages and literature to attract hires in care & support workers 
in Childrens’ Services, have proven effective to increase applications
• Induction processes improved across Group
• Group has dedicated training resource and programme that can deliver basic compliance training
Difficulties in recruitment & training 
have hampered growth
High
Strategy & Performance
Failure to develop, execute and operationalise  
a strategic plan that ensures continued  
viable growth
• High levels of indebtedness inhibit the Group’s ability to achieve 
long-term growth ambitions
• Reduced strategic flexibility due to need to manage business  
within terms of revised bank facilities
• Loss of shareholder and other stakeholder confidence
• Annual budgeting process sets KPI goals for each service
• Each service conducts regular individual performance reviews with Operations Directors/
Regional Managers to monitor all aspects of performance
• Strategy focused on fill out of existing new capacity
• Weekly senior management meeting to monitor performance
High levels of indebtedness lead to  
a requirement to consider strategic 
options to reduce borrowings
High
Integration
Failure to realise the benefits and synergies of 
effectively integrating new sites and acquisitions
• Failure to achieve economies of scale
• Additional costs incurred for running separate operating divisions
• Decrease in efficiency of operations
• Acquisition opportunities assessed on fit with Cambian, their growth potential and their current 
performance (commercial, legal and financial due diligence)
• Integration timetable developed for all acquisitions (delayed integration agreed for new 
acquisitions due to current systems immaturity)
• Review of acquisition progress within the first 12 months
Medium
Business Change
We fail to effectively deliver the key business  
change programmes
• Financial loss 
• Additional time and resources required for manual work-arounds
• Reduced ability for future growth
• Regulatory breach
• Major internal control failing
• Small focused team engaged to deliver process improvements identified in the design phase  
of the business change programme
The Group’s revised approach is to 
seek to improve the existing systems 
and processes, rather than implement 
a new solution
Medium
Government Action
We fail to anticipate and/or have a timely 
response to sudden changes in government 
policy or regulation
• Additional cost burdens are placed on our business
• Some or all of our existing services have to be closed,  
either permanently or, until they can be re-configured 
• We suffer significant reductions in demand for our services
• Intelligence gathered by senior management from press and other sources on proposed 
legislative and regulatory changes
• Strategy day to consider anticipated regulatory/legislative changes
The Group was able to pass through 
price increases during 2015 and has 
plans for pass through of cost associated 
with National Living Wage in 2016
Medium

and uncertainties that may affect the  
Group and highlights the mitigating  
actions that are being taken.

Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 31
Strategic report Performance review
Adult Services
Overview
Adult Services revenue grew by 20% in  
the year including the contribution from 
Woodleigh, acquired in December 2014. 
Average occupancy was 87% (2014: 89%), 
the reduction mainly being the impact of 
the new places opened in the year being 
at the start of their maturity profile. Over 
the year, Adult Services added 43 net new 
occupants organically, a relatively modest 
number, but this follows a strong 
performance in 2014. 
The primary areas of growth were in 
Personality Disorders and Acquired Brain 
Injury. As new units mature we expect to 
increase occupancy further in the future. 
Adjusted EBITDA margin was 20.6% (2014: 
24.5%), reflecting the impact of growth sites 
in the year, some additional costs in our 
mature Adult sites, and additional support 
costs in areas such as HR and Quality.
Growth
The Adult Services market is more mature 
than the Children’s market. However,  
we see opportunities in specialist sub-
segments in the Adult market and, to  
that end, we opened four larger units  
in Adult in the year with including two 
Personality Disorder units, an Acquired 
Brain Injury unit and a unit for Adults  
with autism. 
We have two Woodleigh units under 
construction and due to open later this 
year and, with a good performance from 
existing Woodleigh units since acquisition 
in 2014, we are confident that there will  
be strong demand for these services.
The focus of our growth plan in the 
year was in the Children’ s division.
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 32 Children’s Services 
Overview
Children’s Services revenue grew by 21%  
in the year, including the contribution of  
By the Bridge in 2015. Average occupancy 
in Children’s Services was 73% (2014: 74%), 
reflecting the relatively immature nature  
of the Children’s Services segment as 
compared to the Adult Services segment, 
and in particular, the significant capacity 
added in 2015. 
Whilst we added 188 net new occupants 
organically in Children’s Services, this was 
short of our target as we were unable to 
accept admissions in some parts of our 
Children’s Services in the second half of  
the year due to staffing and training  
issues, and the relatively short tenure of 
new staff recruited. Our autism schools 
and Children’s mental health services  
saw good growth in occupancy with new 
capacity added in the year. 
The Adjusted EBITDA margin of Children’s 
Services was 10.4% (2014: 17.0%), with an 
absolute reduction in Adjusted EBITDA of 
£6.1m. The biggest impact on profit was 
within our Children’s residential services 
where we incurred significant additional 
costs in areas such as wages, recruitment 
and repairs and maintenance, without  
a commensurate increase in revenue. 
Against this our education and Children’s 
mental health units grew profitability in  
the year. In addition, profitability was 
impacted by significant additional central 
support costs in the year, for example  
in the operations teams required to 
manage a portfolio of over 200 sites.
Growth 
The focus of our growth plan in the year 
was in the Children’s division.
We increased our education services 
significantly, in particular adding three 
large schools: Bletchley, Spring Hill and 
Potterspury Lodge (with a combined 
capacity of 166 places). These offer 
significant opportunity for future revenue 
growth as we build capacity and focus 
their offerings on higher value services to 
address more acute needs. We have also 
grown our Children’s residential services, in 
particular for children suffering from abuse 
or neglect or with mental health conditions. 
We have previously highlighted fostering 
as an area that we wished to grow. To  
this end, we were pleased to acquire By 
the Bridge in March. By the Bridge operates 
at the high-severity end of fostering and 
has built a reputation for providing high 
quality, therapeutic fostering services  
and for successfully placing children with 
complex needs in a family environment. As 
such, it occupies a niche position between 
traditional fostering and residential care 
and now forms an integral part of our 
Children’ Services offering. Cambian’s 
existing fostering operation has been 
integrated into By the Bridge during the 
year. Our focus is now on foster carer 
recruitment to drive placement numbers. 
At 31 December 2015 the Group had  
668 fostering placements (2014: 203 
placements), of which 501 related to  
By the Bridge. 
 
 
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 33
Strategic report Finance review
Group performance 
In 2015 the Group delivered revenue 
growth of 21% (2014: 12%). Average 
occupancy was 78% (2014: 81%) the drop 
largely being due to the lag effect of new 
places added in the year. The Group’s 
Adjusted EBITDA
1
 margin was 14.7% (2014: 
20.1%), impacted by additional costs being 
incurred in the year. At a unit level, costs 
were incurred particularly in relation to 
new sites in areas such as recruitment 
costs, in advance of revenue growth from 
occupancy. In addition, we increased  
costs centrally, including in our operations 
teams, HR function and sales and 
marketing function, which impacted  
the margin in the year in both Adult  
and Children’s services. 
With the scaling back of the Group’s  
growth plan, Underlying EBITDA  
(calculated as Adjusted EBITDA adding 
back development losses, being losses 
incurred in the first 18 months of a site’s 
operation or repositioning) is no longer  
a KPI that is being measured. Instead, 
Adjusted EBITDA is the key measure  
of business profitability.
Operating profit 
Adjusted EBITDA reconciles to Operating 
Profit as follows:
M&A costs
M&A costs represent advisory fees, stamp 
duty and other direct costs in respect of 
acquisitions completed in the year. 
Charge on IPO option plans
The charge on IPO option plans arises on 
Continuation Option Plan shares awarded 
as part of the IPO, the impact of which is 
excluded from Adjusted EBITDA. Charges 
on future share based awards will be 
included within Adjusted EBITDA.
Exceptional items 
Exceptional items consist of a fixed asset 
impairment of £21.7m, £2.7m IT project 
costs written off, redundancy costs of 
£0.3m and IT integration costs of £0.2m. 
The fixed asset impairment relates to 19 
sites where the net asset value was not 
supported by the value in use or fair value 
less costs of disposal.
IT project costs written off relate to  
£0.9m costs capitalised in 2014, and 
£1.8m of costs capitalised in 2015, in 
relation to an integrated Finance, HR  
and CRM system. In December 2015  
the Board revised the project in order  
to pursue a lower cost option of 
remediating current systems.
Finance charges
The Group incurred net finance costs  
of £8.8m in the year (2014: £11.4m).
Taxation 
The Group’s tax charge was a credit  
£6.8m (2014: £4.1m charge). This includes  
a credit of £8.5m in relation to the 
impairment of assets and a revaluation  
of deferred tax liabilities following the 
change in the UK corporation tax rate. 
Excluding these factors, the Group’s tax  
rate was 22% of profit before tax and  
M&A and exceptional costs. The difference 
between the current statutory rate of 20.25% 
and the effective tax rate is principally due  
to non-deductible expenditure and 
non-qualifying depreciation. 
Earnings per share 
Statutory basic EPS was a loss of 5.4 pence 
(2014: loss of 6.1 pence), and statutory 
diluted EPS was a loss of 5.4 pence (2014: 
loss of 6.1 pence). Adjusted basic EPS is 
defined as statutory basic EPS, adding 
back the impact of amortisation of 
acquired intangible assets, the charge 
relating to Continuation Option Plan  
shares awarded as part of the IPO,  
and exceptional items and M&A costs,  
net of the tax effect of these items.

Acquisitions 
During the year, the Group acquired By the Bridge for a net cash consideration of £34.3m, initially funded by debt and subsequently 
partially refinanced through an issue of additional share capital raising £25.4m. 
In addition, the Group purchased the share capital of Interact Care Limited, a portfolio of assets providing Learning Disability services  
to Children, for a net cash consideration of £3.3m, and acquired two schools, Spring Hill and Potterspury Lodge for £1.6m and £2.1m 
respectively. For the purposes of the capacity and occupancy numbers within this report, these purchases are treated as organic growth  
as the assets were acquired at rebuild cost and meet our organic growth capital expenditure hurdle rates of return. 
Capital expenditure 
The Group incurred £44.3m (2014: £24.5m) of capital expenditure in the year, of which £32.5m was spent on acquiring and developing 
new capacity. A further £6.8m (2014: £5.2m) was spent on the maintenance of our existing units (including £0.6m remedial work on 
certain Woodleigh units), £1.8m was incurred on an integrated Finance, HR and CRM project (which was cancelled in December 2015  
as the Group pursued remediation of current systems), and £3.1m was spent on IT and non-site level capital expenditure, including 
refurbishing our central office in Hammersmith.

Strategic report The movement on working capital 
comprises a £17.6m outflow on the 
movement on trade and other debtors,  
a £6.2m inflow from the movement on 
deferred income and £3.0m inflow on 
trade and other payables. The increase  
in trade and other debtors partly arises 
from an acceleration in the timing of 
billing of certain of our services in 2015 
and is effectively offset by the increase  
in deferred income. Netting these two 
factors gives a net outflow of £11.4m from 
trade and other receivables – a reduction 
from the position reported in our 2015  
half year results, but still a higher than 
expected outflow given the growth in the 
business in the year. The reason for this 
was issues arising out of the integration  
of the finance functions of Cambian  
and Advanced Childcare during 2015. 
During the year, the Group made tax 
payments of £8.3m which related to  
the prior year charge, and instalment 
payments on our current year charge. 
In March 2015, following the acquisition of 
By the Bridge, the Group issued 11,863,636 
shares for a cash consideration of £25.4m, 
net of fees. 
Debt Facilities 
The Group extended its facilities agreement 
in March 2015 by £35m initially to fund the 
acquisition of By the Bridge. In the second 
half of 2015, the Group entered into £80m  
of interest rate swaps until April 2019 at  
a blended rate of 1.6% over LIBOR. 
At 31 December 2015, the total facilities 
available to the Group were £290m of which 
£256.5m was utilised. Together with cash 
and other debt like items on the balance 
sheet, net debt was £239.3m (2014: £188.7m). 
On 26 April the Board and the Group’s 
lending banks agreed terms for the 
amendment of the Group’s £290m Facilities 
Agreement, the principal provisions of which 
are that a fee of £2.9m (representing 1% of 
the total Facilities) is payable immediately, 
with a flat rate margin of 3.75% over LIBOR 
payable on the amounts drawn under the 
Facilities. Furthermore, the Facilities are split 
into “Tranche A” of £120m and “Tranche B”  
of £170m. Additional interest of 10% per year 
is to be accrued on Tranche A and paid on 
repayment or expiry of Tranche A. Should 
Tranche A not be repaid by 30 April 2017 , then 
a further fee of £4.0m is payable. An exit fee 
of up to £10m is payable on repayment of 
Tranche A which expires on 30 September 
2017 . Tranche B expires on 31 March 2019. The 
Group has also amended its covenants and 
a number of information undertakings under 
the agreed terms.
An important requirement of the agreed 
amended terms is the repayment of Tranche 
A by 30 September 2017 . As explained in the 
Chairman’s statement on page 6, the Board 
has been actively reviewing with its advisors 
a number of strategic options for the Group 
and the Board is confident that these will 
enable a successful repayment by that date.
Dividend 
In view of the disappointing financial 
performance of the business in the year,  
as announced on 9 February 2016, the 
Board has determined that no dividend  
will be proposed in respect of the 2015 
financial year.

and viability statement
Going concern statement
The directors have considered the Group’s 
financial resources including a review of 
the medium-term financial plan, which 
includes a review of the Group’s cash  
flow forecasts for the period of at least  
12 months from the date of approval of 
these financial statements. The directors 
reviewed the assumptions that underlie  
the cash-flow forecasts produced by 
management and tested these under  
a number of differing scenarios
In particular, the directors have considered 
the availability of cash, short-term deposits 
and undrawn facilities under committed 
facilities of £290m, which, when taken  
out, were due to mature on 31 March 2019. 
Since the end of the financial year, as 
described on page 36 of the finance review 
and as set out in note 35 to the financial 
statements, the Company has agreed 
terms for amendment of these facilities  
(the “Amended Facilities”). 
The directors believe that the Group will  
be able to draw down on the Amended 
Facilities, if required to finance the Group’s 
forecast cash requirements during the 
period under review. This provides 
confidence that the Group has sufficient 
financial resources for at least 12 months 
from the date of approval of these financial 
statements. As a consequence, the 
directors believe that the Company is  
well placed to manage its business. 
Based on the considerations noted  
above, the directors have a reasonable 
expectation that the Company and the 
Group have adequate resources to 
continue in operational existence for  
at least 12 months from the date of 
approval of these financial statements.  
For this reason, the directors continue  
to adopt the going concern basis in 
preparing the accounts.
Viability statement
In accordance with the revised UK 
Corporate Governance Code, the directors 
have assessed the prospects of the Group 
over a period significantly longer than 12 
months from 31 December 2015. 
The directors have concluded that the  
most appropriate time period for this 
review should be a three year period  
to 31 December 2018. This period of 
assessment has been chosen since  
it conforms with the Group’s strategic  
plan and the term of the Amended 
Facilities as set out in note 35 to the 
financial statements.
In making their assessment, the directors 
considered, in particular, Cambian’s  
ability to repay the £120m tranche of  
the Amended Facilities during 2017.  
The directors formed the view that there  
were reasonable grounds for concluding 
that the Group would be able to meet this 
obligation under the Amended Facilities in 
the light of the options open to the Group 
following a strategic review undertaken 
with its financial advisers and the quality 
of, and continued demand for, the services 
provided by the Group.
In addition, the directors reviewed the 
current financial and operational position 
and contracted and forecast capital 
expenditures of the Group during the 
period. The directors also tested the 
assumptions underlying the Group’s 
business plans under a variety of 
scenarios, including the likelihood of 
delivering on the current strategy of  
the Group to complete and fill the new 
facilities it has in development. They  
also assessed the potential financial and 
operational impacts of the principal risks  
and uncertainties set out on pages 30  
and 31, together with the current controls, 
assurances and mitigating factors that 
could reduce the impact of such risks.  
The directors also gave consideration  
to the impact of the introduction of the 
National Living Wage on the Group’s  
cost base and the ability of the Group  
to pass on any increased costs through 
planned fee increases or to otherwise 
mitigate its impact. 
Based on this assessment, the directors 
have a reasonable expectation that the 
Company and the Group will be able  
to continue in operation and meet their 
liabilities as they fall due through to the 
end of 2018.
