Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 38 Being a successful and 
sustainable business 
requires Cambian to  
do more than generate  
a financial return  
for our shareholders.  
We believe our continued 
success depends on 
acknowledging and  
fulfilling our responsibilities 
to those individuals who  
are entrusted to our care,  
to our employees and  
our other stakeholders.
As a leading provider of specialist 
behavioural health services for adults  
and children in the UK, we believe our 
most important corporate responsibility is 
to continue to deliver successful outcomes 
for the individuals entrusted to our care, so 
that they can each achieve their personal 
best. We do this by ensuring that our staff 
and systems are focused on the delivery  
of good-quality, therapeutically led services 
in modern, high-quality facilities or within 
well-supported, outstanding foster families 
that deliver outcomes leading to a better 
quality of life for our service users. In the 
year we celebrated the achievements of  
a young person in our fostering services 
publishing a book through Matador  
and another from Grately House School 
being offered a place to study at 
Cambridge University.
Corporate Social Responsibility (“CSR”)  
also permeates how we treat our over 
7,000 employees and give them the 
training and support to continue to 
deliver excellent care, as well as our 
commitment to playing a positive role in  
the communities we serve and in how  
we manage our environmental impacts.
Our Group Code of Conduct
Our Code of Conduct provides the 
framework for our policies, programmes 
and procedures for a range of Corporate 
Responsibility issues. It sets out broad 
principles based on the common values  
of responsibility, accountability, integrity, 
honesty, fairness and transparency. 
This gives us a clear understanding of  
how we do business and how we work 
with each other and those in our care, as  
well as with other stakeholders. It applies  
to every Cambian employee and it applies  
to every interaction we make. 
This year we began a review of our core 
values and Code of Conduct to make  
sure they reflect our diverse and growing 
business, while being aligned to our core 
purpose: to be one of the largest providers 
of specialist behavioural health services for 
children and adults in the UK. More work  
is being done in 2016 to bring together a 
Cambian culture with shared values and 
common goals. 
Social and community involvement
Cambian is focused on developing strong 
ties with the local communities in which  
we are situated. It helps both foster an 
understanding in the community of the 
work that we do and has therapeutic and 
educational benefits for those individuals  
in our care. There are numerous examples 
of community participation, such as: 
• A number of local football teams are 
supported by Cambian facilities, such  
as the support that Delfryn House and 
Delfryn Lodge provide to local football 
team, Mold Alexandra
• Within our educational services,  
a number of schools and colleges  
make their facilities available where 
practicable for local use, such as  
the New Elizabethan School in 
Worcestershire which makes its cricket 
pitch available for the local cricket club
• Cambian Dilston College has formed  
a local partnership with Darlington 
College. Working in conjunction with the 
college, we provide life skills training to 
local students, preparing them for more 
independent living. We also work with 
them to develop their employability skills; 
this includes supporting students on a 
local work placement. The partnership 
also involves a tutor from the college 
providing tutoring services to locals four 
days a week
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 39
Strategic report • We submit entries annually in the 
Koestler Awards, a national art 
competition recognising the creative 
talents of people in secure settings.  
The awards aim to create a positive  
goal that entrants can strive towards.  
By participating, it is hoped they will 
benefit from gaining recognition for  
their achievements, with regional and 
national exhibitions providing a chance  
to get entrants’ artwork seen by the 
public and opportunities for sales
• We are keen supporters of national 
campaigns and events such as  
National Autism Week and Foster  
Care Fortnight
• Elston House took part in a week  
long national campaign to raise money 
for the National Autistic Society. From  
27 March to 2 April, 2015, a number  
of ‘extra-curricular’ activities were 
organised with one common theme, 
‘Stand out for Autism’. The week 
culminated in a ‘Night Walk’, with  
a large contingency of followers, 
residents and Cambian team members 
marching through the quiet streets of  
the village of Elston
• We actively encourage all people  
within the Group to support local and 
national charities through fundraising 
activities such as charity bake sales  
and clothing donations
• The Group funds two free places at  
its schools: one in its schools for pupils  
with autism and one for pupils with 
Asperger’s Syndrome
A key component of our Corporate 
Responsibility programme relates to 
ensuring that our business activities are 
conducted in such a way that we are not 
complicit in the abuse of fundamental 
human rights and labour rights. This is  
a particular issue with the services which 
Cambian provides to adults and children 
who may have mental health issues  
or intellectual difficulties that make the  
issues of consent to treatment particularly 
sensitive. The Group places particular 
emphasis through training and policies 
that before any individuals in our care 
receive any care or treatment they are 
asked for their consent and the provider 
acted in accordance with their wishes,  
or where people do not have the  
capacity to consent, the provider acted  
in accordance with legal requirements.
Employees
Our people are at the heart of our 
business; they are central to the quality  
of care and support we offer to those 
entrusted to us. The pursuit of talent  
in the care sector remains a challenge,  
so the recruitment, retention and 
development of our people continue  
to be a key priority for the Group. 
Following a comprehensive review of the 
Group’s HR and talent strategy, we took  
a new approach to recruitment this year  
to help build the best talent pool and lay 
solid foundations for a working culture 
across the business:
We identified what good looks like
• We’ve standardised role profiles  
across the Group with a clear outline  
of accountabilities, required experience 
and skills
We changed the way we source 
candidates
• Along with enhancing our direct  
sourcing channels (reducing our  
reliance on costly recruitment agencies), 
we are undertaking proactive searches  
for passive candidates with greater  
use of referrals
We are attracting the right people
• We’ve put together a strong employer 
brand and are attracting people who 
want meaningful work and are trusted  
to do a good job
We’ve changed how we select candidates
• We are looking to recruit people with 
motivation and passion for a career in 
care, not just look at their experience
We’ve introduced a new approach to 
inducting colleagues
• We communicate with candidates prior 
to them joining to fully engage them  
with the organisation
These initiatives, along with the 
establishment of a HR Shared Services 
Centre to focus on recruitment, will 
enhance our efforts to create and foster  
a strong workplace culture, with further 
plans to continue this work in 2016.
The Group’s policy is that it will not tolerate 
any discrimination, directly or indirectly,  
in recruitment or employment because of 
age, disability, sex, gender reassignment, 
pregnancy, maternity, race (which includes 
colour, nationality and ethnic or national 
origins), sexual orientation, religion or 
belief, or because someone is married or 
in a civil partnership. We will demonstrate 
our commitment by:
• Promoting equal opportunity for our 
current and potential team members
• Reflecting the communities in which  
we work
• Aiming to build teams which reflect the 
diversity of our customers and treating 
our customers, partners and team 
members fairly and with respect
• Promoting an environment free from 
discrimination, bullying and harassment, 
and tackling any behaviour which may 
breach this intent
• Providing support and encouragement 
to our people to develop their careers and 
increase their contribution to Cambian

This section includes our mandatory 
reporting of greenhouse gas emissions 
pursuant to the Companies Act 2006 
(Strategic Report and Directors’ Report 
Regulations 2013) (the “Regulations”). We 
include this reporting data in this section  
in order to provide a complete Corporate 
Responsibility picture.
Reporting year
We have aligned our greenhouse gas 
emissions reporting year with our  
financial year, being 1 January 2015 to  
31 December 2015.
Greenhouse gas emissions (GHG) 
reporting
We have reported on all of the emission 
sources required under the Large and 
Medium-Sized Companies and Groups 
(Accounts and Reports) Regulations 2008 
as amended in August 2013. 
Reporting boundary
The reporting boundary used for collation of 
the above data is consistent with that used 
for consolidation purposes in the financial 
statements. We report our emissions data 
using an operational control approach to 
define our organisational boundary which 
meets the definitional requirements of the 
Regulations in respect of those emissions for 
which we are responsible. We have reported 
We have continued to make a concerted 
effort to reduce our carbon footprint. For 
example, across our business we have 
continued to focus on the reduction of 
emissions by:
• Implementing vehicle tracking on fleet 
vehicles to promote less aggressive  
and more fuel efficient driving strategies
• Adopting new more energy-efficient 
standards and specifications for the 
building of new facilities and conversions 
of buildings that we acquire and aim  
to achieve minimum BREEAM standards 
wherever possible
• Implementation of a range of energy 
efficiency projects including the 
introduction of more energy efficient 
condenser boilers into our facilities  
and better insulation specifications  
at all sites and unless prohibited by 
Listed Building or Conservation Areas
• Promoting the use of rail travel
on all material emission sources for which 
we deem ourselves to be responsible. These 
sources align with our operational control 
and financial control boundaries. We do  
not have responsibility for any emission 
sources that are beyond the boundary of  
our operational control. For example, 
business travel other than by car (including, 
for example, commercial flights) is not within 
our operational control and, therefore, is not 
considered to be our responsibility.
Methodology
The greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions  
report has been prepared in line with UK 
mandatory reporting requirements, set  
by the Department for Environment, Food 
and Rural Affairs (DEFRA). The mandatory 
requirement is for the disclosure of scope  
1 and 2 emissions only. These are direct 
emissions such as heating, vehicle fuel and 
indirect emissions, for example purchased 
gas and electricity. The Group’s total GHG 
footprint in line with DEFRA’s mandatory 
reporting requirements is 15.5m tonnes CO
2
e.
Intensity ratio
In order to express our annual emissions in 
relation to a quantifiable factor associated 
with our activities, we have used revenue 
in our intensity ratio calculation, as this is 
the most relevant indication of our growth 
and provides for a good comparative 
measure over time.

Dear Shareholder
Introduction
Corporate governance at Cambian  
is about running the business in the  
right way in order to create long-term 
sustainable value for the benefit of all of 
our stakeholders: the adults and children 
placed under our care, their families, our 
commissioners, our regulators and our 
shareholders. I hope that by reading our 
governance reports you will gain a better 
understanding of our culture and the 
effectiveness of our Board.
What good governance means  
to Cambian 
Corporate governance at Cambian is 
treated as a core and vital discipline that 
complements our need to improve the 
performance of the business on behalf  
of our service users, commissioners and 
shareholders. Our approach to governance 
is set by the Board. Our executive board 
then ensures that our approach is effectively 
implemented across the entire business, 
and that all our employees are aware of, 
and live by, our culture and uphold the 
highest standards of service. We believe 
that effective governance is achieved 
through leadership and collaboration, 
resulting in consistently focused and 
sensible business decisions
Board performance in 2015
Non-executive site visits
The independent role of our non-executive 
directors is extremely important to us.  
We are determined to ensure that they  
can play an active role in the development 
and management of our business. We do 
not believe they can develop a complete 
picture of how the Group operates by  
simply reviewing Board papers and 
attending Board and committee meetings.

meetings with commissioners.

open and candid about issues facing 
the business and clearer about its 
recommendations and decision making. 
We can achieve this through greater 
and more regular exposure to the 
executive board members.
(iv) Our systems and processes need to 
be reviewed and, where necessary, 
overhauled to ensure that we are able 
accurately to record and forecast the 
financial performance of our business, 
and we are implementing remedial 
actions in these areas.
(v) A comprehensive set of key 
performance indicators (KPI’s) should 
be developed and understood at  
all levels of the business. These  
have been developed and cover 
measurements such as revenue per 
bed, profitability, average length of 
stay, and clinical quality.
Board experience
To achieve its governance objectives, the 
Board comprises a majority of independent 
non-executive directors who have been 
selected to deliver an appropriate mix of 
diversity, skills and experience. The Board 
is led by an independent Chairman, who  
in turn is well-supported by a Senior 
Independent Director. 
 
I am delighted that Mike Butterworth has 
agreed to join the Board as an independent 
non-executive director and his considerable 
experience as CFO in a number of listed 
companies will be a considerable asset to 
Cambian. Further details of the Board can 
be found on pages 44 and 45.
Board committees
At the time of our 2014 Annual Report, the 
Board had formed four committees: Audit, 
Remuneration, Nomination and a Quality 
and Risk Committee under the guidance of 
its then Chair, Anne Marie Carrie. Anne Marie 
Carrie decided to stand down in March 2015 
as a non-executive director in order to 
become the CEO of our Children’s Services 
division. At the same time, the Board 
considered how it could most effectively 
discharge its responsibilities under the UK 
Corporate Governance Code, as amended in 
September 2014 (the “Code”) for monitoring 
We have therefore implemented a 
programme of individual site visits whereby 
each of our non-executives is required to visit 
at least one site independently during the 
year. These visits give our non-executive 
directors a valuable opportunity to meet 
and engage with our local management 
teams to understand better local operations 
and procedures and to get to know our 
people and those they care for.
Induction of new NED
We were delighted to welcome Dr Graham 
Rich as an independent non-executive 
director in July 2015 who brought a  
wealth of experience as a clinician  
and management consultant within  
the healthcare sector. In conjunction  
with the Company Secretary, we provided  
a tailored induction programme designed  
to ensure that Graham obtained a 
comprehensive picture of Cambian’s 
operations and culture. 
Performance evaluation
The Board appointed Lintstock Limited,  
an independent consultancy, to assist us  
in the annual Board evaluation which was 
conducted with the assistance of the Company 
Secretary by me in October and November 
2015. The process consisted of a carefully 
prepared online questionnaire which  
was completed by both the Board and  
the executive board. The answers to the 
questionnaires were then compiled and 
discussed at a meeting of the non-executive 
directors on 12 November 2015 and a final 
version was approved with recommendations 
to the Board on 15 December 2015.
The principal conclusions and 
recommendations were that:
(i) The Board composition of five 
non-executive directors (one of whom 
is not independent) and two executive 
directors is adequate but we should 
look to add a further non-executive 
director with relevant public company 
experience in 2016 and I am delighted 
that we announced the appointment 
of Mike Butterworth to the Board.
(ii) The Board needs to develop greater 
understanding of both our staff and 
our commissioning customers. This 
can best be achieved through the 
independent site visits described

Section of The Code Further information
Leadership
A company must be led by an effective board responsible for the success of 
the company, in the near and long term. Such a board will have clear divisions 
of responsibility between company governance and business execution. 
Board leadership, 
p.46
Effectiveness
The established board will have the relevant level of and appropriate 
balance of skills in order to suitably steer the company. Such knowledge  
is certified by rigorous procedures regarding the appointment of new,  
and the re-appointment of existing, Directors.
Evaluation,  
p.49
Accountability
At all times, the board must present a fair, balanced and understandable 
evaluation of the company’s standing and future prospects. Such future 
prospects are considered against risks that the company is or may face 
moving forward; it is the Board’s responsibility to ensure effective and 
appropriate risk management procedures are in place. 
Strategic report 
p.2 to 41
Remuneration
While it is necessary for levels of remuneration to attract, retain and motivate 
directors of sufficient quality, at no point should the company allocate more  
than is necessary. Where possible, remuneration should be linked to 
performance and, at all times, established through formal and transparent 
procedures of which no one director is involved in his or her own remuneration. 
Directors 
remuneration 
report, p.59 to 74
Relations with Shareholders
The board is responsible for ensuring a clear, coherent and regular 
dialogue with shareholders at all times.
Relations with 
shareholders, p.50

report the totality of all risks across of the 
Group into the Audit Committee, so as to 
create a single point for assisting the Board  
in its obligations under the Code, and to 
rename the Audit Committee as the Audit & 
Risk Committee. The composition and terms 
of reference of the committees of the Board  
are described in more detail below.

How we govern the Company
Our governance structure comprises  
the functions shown below, supported  
by the Group’s policies and controls.
Executive Management Committee
The Executive Management Committee oversees the 
development of the Group’s services against budget; 
monitors levels of occupancy across the Group and 
the progress of new service openings; seeks to 
share best clinical and safeguarding practice across 
the Group; and monitors and reports against the 
Group’s risk management framework.

Disclosure Committee
The Disclosure Committee meets, as required,  
to consider the disclosure of information by the 
Group as required by the Disclosure and 
Transparency Rules.
Clinical Governance Committee
The Clinical Governance Committee reviews reports 
from the internal quality assurance team, analyses 
the level of reported incidents across the Group, 
considers operational best practice and reviews any 
recent regulatory inspections and any regulatory 
concerns or weaknesses identified.
Board
The Board has collective 
responsibility for the management, 
direction and performance of the 
Company and provides leadership 
within a framework of prudent  
and effective controls. The Board 
sets the strategic direction of the 
Company and takes a long-term 
outlook, seeing itself as responsible 
to the Group’s stakeholders, 
including shareholders, service 
users, care commissioning bodies 
and employees.

Governance UK Corporate Governance Compliance statement
In September 2014, the Financial Reporting Council published the 
2014 edition of the UK Corporate Governance Code (the “Code”) 
which contains broad principles and specific provisions to assist 
how boards operate. This Code applied to Cambian during the 
financial year ended 31 December 2015.
In the period following the resignation of Anne Marie Carrie and 
before the appointment of Dr Graham Rich in July 2015, at least half 
the Board, excluding the chairman, did not comprise non-executive 
directors determined by the Board to be independent, as required by 
Code provision B.1.2, and the Audit Committee only comprised two 
independent non-executive directors, Alison Halsey and Chris 
Brinsmead, which was only appropriate for smaller quoted 
companies (Code Provision C.3.1).
In addition, as disclosed in the directors’ remuneration report on 
pages 59 to 74, certain nil-cost option awards were made to executive 
directors (all of which were made prior to Admission) which will vest  
as to one-third of the award on each of the third, fourth,and fifth 
anniversaries of the date of Admission. These awards do not contain 
any performance-related vesting conditions as recommended in 
Schedule A of the Code since they were made prior to Admission  
and in part to reward for past performance and to provide a  
long-term retention mechanism for the executive directors and  
key senior managers.
Save as disclosed above, the Board considers that it has complied 
with the provisions of the Code throughout the year. The tables 
below set out our approach to applying the Code.
Board leadership
Role of the Board 
The Board has collective responsibility for the management, 
direction and performance of the Company and provides 
leadership within a framework of prudent and effective controls 
which seeks to enable risk to be appropriately assessed and 
managed. The Board has established the governance framework 
illustrated in the chart on page 43 to support the development  
of good governance practices throughout the Group.
The Board takes a long-term outlook and sees itself as responsible 
to a wide range of stakeholders, including shareholders, customers, 
care commissioning bodies and employees, whilst pursuing its 
objectives in a manner consistent with its statutory duties.
Board composition and balance 
As at 31 December 2015, the Board comprised the Chairman,  
the Chief Executive Officer, the Chief Financial Officer, together  
with three independent non-executive directors and one further 
non-executive director. 
Corporate governance report
The list of current directors, their responsibilities and respective 
dates of appointment are set out in the table below.
Director’s name Title Appointed

Further biographical information on each of our directors can be 
found on pages 44 and 45, which shows the breadth of strategic 
and financial management insight brought to our Board. All of our 
independent non-executive directors have held senior executive 
or non-executive positions within listed companies. These 
non-executive directors bring industry experience from a wide 
range of backgrounds including finance, business services, 
pharmaceuticals, software and the NHS.
The principle of boardroom diversity is strongly supported by the 
Board. It is the Board’s policy that appointments will always be 
based on merit so that the Board has the right individuals in place. 
The Board ensures that diversity is an important consideration and 
part of the selective criteria used to assess candidates to achieve 
a balanced board.
The Board also reviews non-executive directors’ independence  
on an annual basis taking into account such factors as their 
contribution to unbiased and independent debate during 
meetings. All non-executive directors (other than Alfred Foglio)  
are considered by the Board to be independent of management 
and free of any relationship, which could materially interfere with 
the exercise of their independent judgement, as explained above. 
Alfred Foglio is not considered to be independent for the purposes 
of the Code as a result of his being the director appointed to  
the Board by GI Partners in accordance with the terms of the 
Relationship Agreement. 
To safeguard their independence, a director is not entitled to vote  
on any matter in which they have a material personal interest 
unless the rest of the Board unanimously decides otherwise. 
Where necessary, directors are required to absent themselves 
from a meeting of the Board while such matters are being 
discussed, although no such situations arose in 2015. The Board 
has an annual process of formally reviewing conflicts disclosed, 
and the authorisations given (including such conditions as the 
Board may determine in each case). Any conflicts or potential 
conflicts considered by the Board and any authorisations given  
are recorded in the Board minutes and in a register of directors’ 
conflicts which is maintained by the Company Secretary.
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 46 Dr Graham Rich joined the Board in July 2015. As part of his 
induction process, Graham Rich has visited Cambian Alders,  
a specialist service for women with a personality disorder, 
Cambian Churchill, a male mental health rehabilitation service  
in London, Cambian Brunel, a new service we are looking to  
open next year, and Cambian Fairviews, to gain insight into  
the therapeutic model which Cambian delivers. Dr Rich has  
also met with a number of the senior management team to  
gain an understanding of the principal risks and uncertainties 
facing the Group, as well as the strategic challenges and 
opportunities faced by Cambian.
Dr Rich also participated with the other non-executive directors  
in a visit to two of the Group’s specialist schools: the Cambian 
Potterspury Lodge School and Cambian Bletchley Park. Cambian 
Potterspury Lodge, is a residential school for young persons aged 
8–18 years old, who have a diagnosis of Asperger’s Syndrome  
or other associated difficulties. Cambian Bletchley Park is a day 
school for students aged 11-17 years old with a diagnosis of 
autism, communication difficulties and related conditions  
that opened in September 2015. The non-executive directors 
broadened their understanding of Cambian’s approach, designed  
to assist the students in developing academic, social and life skills 
that will enable them to achieve the maximum amount of 
independence in their adult lives, through meeting students, 
teachers, clinicians and other support staff at these facilities.
How the Board functions
The Board meets regularly, with six scheduled meetings held  
in 2015. In addition, three other meetings were held outside this 
schedule, principally related to the approval of the acquisition  
of By the Bridge Limited and its financing, the approval of an 
updated forecast for the Company’s financial performance,  
and to approve the initial stage of a project to improve the 
Company’s financial, HR and sales & marketing processes. 
During the current year, the Board has met regularly in connection 
with the negotiation of the amended terms of the Group’s facility 
agreement and to review the Group’s strategy and options to 
reduce borrowings. During 2016 it is intended that at least two  
of the meetings of the Board will be held at one of the Group’s 
regional management centres in order to ensure that all directors 
have the opportunity to meet regional management teams, to 
broaden their knowledge of the Group’s operations and of the 
industry in general. 
During the year, meetings of the Board were often preceded by  
a board dinner to which members of the executive management 
team or others were invited. These dinners provide a useful  
forum for additional debate between directors and executives  
on complex matters to be discussed at the scheduled meetings.  
This helps the directors to fully understand the issues at hand,  
and ensures that the process of the formal meetings is facilitated.
During the year, the Chairman met the other non-executives in the 
absence of the executive directors to re-confirm and take account 
of their views. 
Roles and responsibilities
The roles of the Chairman (Christopher Kemball) and the  
Chief Executive Officer (Saleem Asaria) are separated  
and clearly defined. The Chairman regularly visits our  
head office in London, and this facilitates frequent interaction, 
discussion and collaboration with the Chief Executive Officer.
The roles and responsibilities of the Board members  
are explained and their respective responsibilities  
summarised below.
Chairman • Overall leadership of the Board;
•  Ensuring the Board as a whole plays a full  
part in the development and determination  
of the Group’s strategic objectives;
•  Ensuring the effectiveness of the Board;
•  Setting the agenda and tone for the Board;
•  Promoting the highest standards of integrity, 
probity and corporate governance throughout 
the Company and particularly at Board level.
Chief Executive 
Officer
•  Executive leadership of the Company’s 
business on a day to day basis;
•  Developing the overall commercial objectives 
of the Group and proposing and developing 
the strategy of the Group in conjunction with 
the Board as a whole;
•  Responsibility, together with his senior 
management team, for the execution of  
the Group’s strategy and implementation  
of Board decisions;
•  Recommendations on senior appointments 
and development of the management team; 
•  Ensuring that the affairs of the Group are 
conducted with the highest standards of 
integrity, probity and corporate governance.
Senior 
Independent 
non-executive 
director
•  Acting as a sounding board for the Chairman;
•  Being available to shareholders if they have 
concerns which cannot be resolved through  
the Chairman or executive management;
•  Acting as an intermediary for the directors 
where necessary;
•  Conducting an annual review of the Chairman’s 
performance.
Non-executive 
directors 
collectively
•  Constructively challenging the executive 
directors;
•  Oversight of the delivery of the Company’s 
strategy within the risk and control frameworks.
Company 
Secretary
•  Ensuring all Board and Board Committee 
meetings are properly held;
•  Assisting the Chairman and CEO in ensuring 
the directors are provided with all relevant 
information;
• Organising directors’ training requirements;
•  Maintaining the Group’s governance and 
listing rule compliance.

Annual Report and Accounts 2015 48 Responsibility and delegation
There remains in place a formal schedule of matters specifically 
reserved for Board consideration and approval, which includes  
the matters set out below:
• Approval of the Group’s long-term objectives and  
commercial strategy;
• Approval of the annual operating and capital expenditure 
budgets and any changes to them;
• Major acquisitions and disposals;
• The extension of the Group’s activities into any new business  
or geographic areas, or to cease any material operations;
• Changes in the Company’s capital structure or entering  
into any material bank facilities or granting security;
• Approval of treasury policies, including foreign currency 
exposures and use of financial derivatives;
• The entering into of agreements that are not in the ordinary course 
of business or material strategically or by reason of their size;
• Changes to the size, composition or structure of the Board  
and its committees; and
• Corporate governance matters.
The Board has delegated certain of its responsibilities to a number 
of committees of the Board to assist in the discharge of its duties. 
The principal committees of the Board currently are the Audit  
& Risk Committee, the Remuneration Committee, and the 
Nomination Committee. The composition of these committees  
is set out in the table on page 43 and a report on the activities  
of each of the committees is set out on pages 52 to 74 below.  
The minutes of each of these committees are circulated to and 
reviewed by the Board. The Company Secretary is secretary to 
each of these committees. The terms of reference for each of  
the committees are available to view on the Company’s website 
www.cambiangroup.com
In addition to an executive management committee, consisting  
of the senior management with responsibility for the operational 
divisions of Children’s Services and Adult Services and by key 
support functions, the Group has established an operational 
governance committee that meets four times per year to monitor 
issues of safeguarding, clinical practice or other operational 
issues. The operational governance committee reports to the  
Audit & Risk Committee of the Board.
Risk
Under the Code, the Board is responsible for determining the 
nature and extent of the principal risks it is willing to take in 
achieving its strategic objectives. The Board should maintain a 
sound system of risk management and internal control systems 
(Main Principle C.2). During the year, the Board carried out an 
assessment of the principal risks facing the Company, including 
those that would threaten its business model, future performance, 
solvency or liquidity. 
During the year and with the assistance of the Audit & Risk 
Committee, the Board have carried out a robust assessment of  
the principal risks facing the Company, including those that would 
threaten its business model, future performance, solvency or 
liquidity. The Board also carried out a review of the effectiveness  
of the Company’s risk management and internal control systems. 
These risks, and the steps taken by Cambian to mitigate them,  
are described more fully on pages 26 to 31. The viability statement 
required to be made under the new Code provision C.2.2. is set 
out on page 37. 
Board balance
The Board comprises individuals with wide business experience 
gained in various industry sectors related to the Group’s business 
and it is the intention of the Board to ensure that the balance of the 
directors reflects the changing needs of the business. 
The Nomination Committee has a formal, rigorous and transparent 
procedure for the appointment of new directors, which are made 
on merit and against objective criteria, having due regard for the 
benefits of diversity, including gender. The Chairman and the rest  
of the Board continue to support Lord Davies’ aspiration for female 
board representation, but this presents a particular challenge for  
a small board. At the start of the year, two of the Group’s Board 
directors (28%) were women, above the 25% recommended by the 
Davies Report, though with the resignation of Anne Marie Carrie 
and the appointment of Dr Graham Rich, this number fell to one. 
Further details on the diversity of the workforce of the Group 
generally are set out on page 38. 
Following a review of the Board’s effectiveness, it was considered 
that it would be strengthened by the appointment of a further 
independent director. While not having a specific policy regarding 
the constitution and balance of the Board, potential new directors 
are considered on their own merits with regards to their skills, 
knowledge, experience and credentials. 
Evaluation
This year’s formal evaluation of the performance of the Board, its 
committees and the individual directors was conducted by Lintstock 
Limited, an external facilitator which has no other connection with 
Cambian. The anonymity of all participants was ensured in order  
to promote the open and frank exchange. Details of the procedure 
adopted for the evaluation and the principal conclusions of the 
review are set out on page 42 in the letter from the Chairman that 
introduces the governance report.
Chris Brinsmead, as Senior Independent Director, led a review of 
the Chairman’s performance through private discussions with the 
remaining directors.
Board tenure
In accordance with the articles of association, every new director 
appointed in the year is required to stand for re-election by 
shareholders at the AGM next following their appointment,  
and at each Annual General Meeting any director who shall have 
been a director at each of the two preceding AGMs shall retire. 
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 49
Governance Notwithstanding the provisions of the articles of association, the 
Board has decided to comply with the Code requirements that 
directors of companies in the FTSE 350 Index submit themselves  
for re-election annually. Therefore, all the directors are seeking 
their re-appointment at this year’s AGM.
The Board has collectively agreed that the directors proposed  
for re-election in 2016 have made significant contributions to the 
business since their last re-election and each has a key role to  
play in the formulation of the Group’s future strategy.
Time commitment and training
All directors are aware of the need to allocate sufficient time to the 
Company in order to discharge their responsibilities effectively. The 
Company provides the non-executive directors with appropriate 
support and facilities for the consideration of the Company’s 
strategy and performance, and a dialogue with the Chairman  
is encouraged so that any issues regarding time pressures or 
conflicting commitments are addressed appropriately. The Board 
monitors the extent of directors’ external interests and any conflicts  
on a continuing basis. The letters of appointment for non-executive 
directors set out the time commitment expected to be necessary to 
perform their duties.
During the year the non-executive directors received a  
number of presentations from the executive directors and senior 
management in relation to the business of the Group, including 
presentations on the services provided by the Group. There  
will be a continued focus during 2016 on ensuring that through  
a combination of presentations, teach-ins and site visits, the 
non-executive directors are provided with sufficient information  
for them to understand fully the challenges and opportunities  
in the services provided by the Group. 
The Chairman consults with the directors on their respective 
training and development requirements. The suitability of external 
courses is kept under review by the Company Secretary who is 
charged with facilitating the induction of new directors and with 
assisting in the ongoing training and development of all directors. 
All directors have access to the advice and services of the 
Company Secretary and a procedure is in place for them to  
take independent professional advice at the Company’s  
expense should this be required.
Information and training provided to directors
The Company Secretary is responsible for ensuring good 
information flows within the Board and its committees and 
between the senior management and the non-executive directors 
and to facilitate the directors in receiving any additional training 
they may require. The Board uses a secure, web-based system 
which provides quick, easy and secure access to Board papers 
and materials. Prior to each Board meeting the directors receive 
through this system the agenda and supporting papers to ensure 
that they have all the latest and relevant information in advance  
of the meeting. After each Board meeting, the Company Secretary 
operates a comprehensive follow-up procedure to ensure that 
actions are completed as agreed by the Board. Directors regularly 
receive additional information from the Company between Board 
meetings, including a monthly Group performance update. Where 
a director was unable to attend a meeting, they were provided 
with all the papers and information relating to that meeting and 
were able to discuss issues arising directly with the Chairman.
Directors’ and officers’ indemnity insurance
The Company recognises that all directors are equally and 
collectively accountable under the law for the proper stewardship  
of the Company’s affairs. The Company maintains a Directors’  
and Officers’ liability insurance policy for the benefit of the 
Company and the directors. 
Relationship with shareholders
The Board is responsible for ensuring that the Company maintains 
a satisfactory dialogue with shareholders. The Chairman and  
the Senior Independent Director are always available to major 
shareholders. Formal trading updates are given to the market 
during the year. Following each of these announcements, 
conference calls are held with shareholders and analysts and  
after the full year and interim results a presentation is made to  
the shareholders and analysts. Analyst research is circulated to  
the Board. A programme of meetings and conference calls is  
also organised at appropriate times during the year at which the  
Chief Executive and Chief Financial Officer comment on Company 
performance and respond to any issues raised by investors. 
Members of the Board, and in particular non-executive directors, 
are kept informed of investors’ views in the main through 
distribution of analysts’ and brokers’ briefings. 
The major shareholders of the Company are listed on page 76  
of the Directors’ Report.
 
Relationship Agreement
The Company’s largest shareholder, GI Partners (“GI”) is one of the 
Group’s founders. In accordance with the requirements of the Listing 
Rules, the Company, GI Partners and GI Partners UK Limited entered 
into a relationship agreement on 11 April 2014 (the “Relationship 
Agreement”). The principal purpose of the Relationship Agreement 
is to ensure that the Company and the Group are capable at all 
times of carrying on their business independently of GI Partners  
and certain persons deemed to be connected with it (together the 
“Potential Controlling Shareholders”) and that agreements and 
transactions with GI Partners and/or any Potential Controlling 
Shareholders will be at arm’s length and on normal commercial 
terms. The Relationship Agreement entitles GI Partners to nominate 
one person to be a director of the Company for so long as the 
Potential Controlling Shareholder, controls at least 10% of the voting 
rights attaching to the ordinary shares of the Company. The current 
nominee is Alfred Foglio.

Annual Report and Accounts 2015 50 Under the Relationship Agreement, GI Partners and GI Partners  
UK have agreed (inter alia) that: 
(i) it will vote its shares in such a manner so as to procure  
that each member of the Group is capable of carrying  
on its business independently of the Potential Controlling 
Shareholders;
(ii) it will not exercise any of the voting rights attaching to its 
shares in such a manner so as to procure any amendment  
to the articles of association which would be inconsistent  
with, undermine or breach any of the provisions of the 
Relationship Agreement; 
(iii) it will not take any action which has or would have the effect 
of preventing the Company or any other member of the Group 
from carrying on its business independently of GI Partners or 
any Potential Controlling Shareholders; 
(iv) it will not take any action which has or would have the effect 
of preventing the Company or any other member of the Group 
from complying with its obligations under the Listing Rules;
(v) it will not exercise any of its voting rights with respect to the 
ordinary shares in a manner that would require the Company 
to operate or make decisions solely for the benefit of any 
member of the GI Group; 
(vi) it will not propose or procure the proposal of a resolution of 
the shareholders (or any class thereof) which is intended or 
reasonably appears to be intended to circumvent the proper 
application of the Listing Rules;
(vii) it will not exercise any of its voting right to vary the articles 
which would: (a) be contrary to the maintenance of the 
Company’s independence (including the Company’s ability to 
operate and make decisions independently of the GI Group); 
(b) prevent the election of Independent Directors; or (c) be 
inconsistent with, undermine or breach any provision of this 
Deed or the Listing Rules; and/or
(viii) it will abstain from voting on any resolution: (a) required  
by paragraph 11.1.7R(3) of the Listing Rules to approve a 
transaction with a related party involving GI Partners or any 
Potential Controlling Shareholders; and (b) proposed by the 
Company in respect of the election or appointment of an 
Independent Director (whether or not the same is required  
by the Listing Rules) where the Company shall have given  
GI Partners written notice requiring it to abstain.
As required by the Listing Rules, the Board reviewed the operation 
of the Relationship Agreement at its meeting in December 2015 
and believes that the Company has complied with its obligations 
under the Relationship Agreement and, so far as the Company is 
aware, the independence provisions included in the Relationship 
Agreement have been complied with during the period under 
review by GI Partners or any Potential Controlling Shareholders. 
The Board believes that the provisions of the Relationship 
Agreement and of Rule 11 of the Listing Rules provide reassurance 
that GI Partners and GI Partners UK will not seek to exercise its 
shareholding capriciously and re-enforces the independence of 
the Company.

Governance Audit & Risk Committee report
Dear Shareholder
I am pleased to give you an overview of the operation and scope 
of the Committee and report on our work over the past year.
The 2014 edition of the UK Corporate Governance Code (the “Code”) 
has placed greater emphasis on risk and the responsibility of 
boards for an organisation’s overall approach to risk. In particular, 
boards are required to ensure the design and implementation of 
appropriate risk management and internal control systems that 
identify the risks facing a company and enable the board to make  
a robust assessment of the principal risks.
In the light of this overall responsibility, the Company’s board  
of directors (the “Board”) undertook a review in the second quarter 
of 2015 of the operation of the Company’s Audit Committee and 
the Quality & Risk Committee over the period from the Company’s 
IPO. Following this review, it was decided to combine the 
responsibilities of the two committees under my chairmanship,  
so as to ensure a single point of reference for the monitoring of 
risk, both clinical and commercial, and reporting to the Board.  
At the same time, the Board agreed amended terms of reference 
for the newly constituted Audit & Risk Committee (“Committee”), 
which are available for review on the Company’s website  
www.cambiangroup.com\investors\governance
As set out on page 26, the Board has overall responsibility  
for determining the nature of the risk it is willing to take and 
ensuring that risks are managed effectively across the Group.  
At the Board’s request, the Committee has reviewed the 
Company’s principal risks in the light of the new provisions of  
the Code, covering the assessment of principal risks. The way  
in which the Company manages risk is set out on pages 26 to  
29 with the principal risks facing the Group set out in pages 30 
and 31. We have reviewed the continuing effectiveness of the 
Company’s risk management processes as part of our review  
of the effectiveness of internal controls.
The Committee recognises the paramount importance of the 
quality of care in all our facilities. Reports on care quality and 
related issues are made to each meeting. Considerable progress has 
been made in formalising governance processes for these 
matters up to Board level.
The Committee has a vital role in providing assurance that the 
financial statements provide a true and fair view of the Group’s 
financial affairs. As part of this assurance, we conduct a review  
of any significant financial judgements made during the year and 
any key financial reporting issues. The Committee concluded that 
we are comfortable with the judgements being made on all of 
these issues. More details can be found on page 54 of this report.
Alison Halsey

Role of the Committee
The Committee’s principal functions are to monitor the integrity  
of the Group’s financial reports; to assist the Board to monitor the 
Company’s risk management and internal control systems and  
to manage the Board’s relationship with the Group’s outsourced 
internal audit team and its external auditors. The functions of the 
Committee are summarised on page 52. 
The Committee’s terms of reference include all relevant  
matters required by Rule 7.1.3 of the Disclosure and Transparency 
Rules and the Code and are available on the Company’s  
website (www.cambiangroup.com) or on request from the 
Company Secretary.
Committee activities
The Committee met five times during the year (including meetings 
of the Quality & Risk Committee) in February, June, August and 
December. All members of the Committee are non-executive 
directors and all are considered by the Board to be independent. 
Its work included:
• Agreeing a strategic risk register for the Company and a 
framework within which to report on and manage risks within 
the business, which sought to capture both business risks and 
risks arising from the quality of care which Cambian delivers.
• Reviewing the contents of the Company’s strategic risk register, 
including the existing systems and controls that were seen as 
providing mitigations to these risks, and the process by which 
the same was compiled.
• Reviewing amended processes for risk management to monitor 
risk both in relation to care quality and clinical matters as well 
business risk generally, in which the Company has been 
supported by work from PwC as an outsourced internal audit 
function which resulted in the framework described on page 56
• Agreeing on the appointment of PwC as internal auditors to the 
Company and their scope of work in the year under review and 
through into the next financial year;
• The establishment of a new independent whistleblowing 
hotline and whistleblowing policy for the Group to  
replace a hotline provided by the Company’s lawyers 
RadcliffesLeBrasseur. The former hotline was not seen as 
being sufficiently independent and had attracted no use  
in the previous 12 months. The new whistleblowing facility  
is operated by Expolink, a well-established provider of 
confidential whistleblowing facilities and allows both 
employees, service users, care commissioners or parents  
to raise issues either by using a dedicated free telephone  
line or online. This arrangement, which has been piloted in  
our educational division, is being rolled out across the Group’s 
divisions. To increase awareness of how to use the system  
to report an issue, our ‘Whistleblowing Policy and Guidelines’ 
were amended to emphasise support for whistleblowers,  
the system’s confidentiality and ease of use.

Annual Report and Accounts 2015 53
Governance and reported their findings to the Committee. The Committee 
was satisfied as a result of the review process that the approach 
taken by the Group in the financial statements was robust.
Value of goodwill & intangible assets
In the light of the Group’s adverse performance against 
expectations in the year, the Committee considered the judgments 
associated with the carrying value of goodwill in the Group’s two 
cash generating units, in particular, the Children’s Services division 
which had experienced poor trading during the year, to determine 
whether there was a risk of material misstatement in carrying 
value and whether an impairment should be recognised. In 
addition, the Committee also considered the judgments made  
in relation to the valuation methodology adopted by management 
to support the carrying value of other intangible assets and the 
investments in subsidiaries, in particular the appropriateness  
of the discount rate applied. The Committee considered the 
assumptions, estimates and judgements made by management 
to support their models that underpin the valuation of intangible 
assets in the balance sheet. The key assumptions applied in the 
calculation relate to the future performance expectations of the 
business unit. Business plans and cash-flow forecasts prepared 
by management supporting the future performance expectations 
used in the valuation were reviewed. In addition, consideration 
was given to independent indicative valuations of the CGU’s 
provided by the Company’s investment bank. The Committee 
received a report on the outcome of the impairment review 
performed by management. The impairment review was also  
an area of focus for the external auditor, who reported its findings 
to the Committee. The Committee satisfied itself that no material 
impairments were required to the carrying value of goodwill. 
Carrying value of property, plant and equipment
In the light of the Group’s trading performance in the year, the 
Committee also considered whether the carrying value of fixed 
assets at loss-making sites could be supported on the basis of a 
comparison of net asset value, value in use or fair value less sale 
cost or whether asset impairments might be required under IAS 
36. The Committee considered management’s assumptions and 
basis of valuation for those assets covered by the review. These 
included valuations, conducted by Knight Frank, of the fair value 
of seven properties in accordance with IFRS 13. The audit plan 
agreed with the external auditors involved a critical evaluation of 
the completeness of management’s impairment review of fixed 
assets. The Committee satisfied itself that the review was robust 
and that an impairment should be made to the carrying value of 
some fixed assets.
• Reviewing the final and interim financial statements and 
matters raised by management and the external auditors. This 
review included consideration of the key judgements applied in 
the preparation of the consolidated financial statements, which 
are described in the relevant accounting policies and detailed in 
the notes to the financial statements on pages 90 to 120.

Significant financial matters
The Committee reviews all significant issues concerning the 
financial statements. The principal matters we considered 
concerning the 2015 financial statements were:
Going concern & viability
The Committee undertook a review, on behalf of the Board, of  
the medium-term and longer-term business plans of the Group  
in order to support the Board’s judgment in relation to the 
preparation of the financial statements on a going concern basis 
and in relation to the viability statement on page 37 . In particular, 
the Committee considered the assumptions that underlay the 
cash-flow forecasts produced by management and tested these 
under a number of differing scenarios. The Committee also 
considered the availability of sources of external finance, if  
required by those forecasts and plans, to support both the 
directors’ going concern statement and the statement on  
longer-term viability set out on page 37 .

The Committee reviewed revenue recognition, in particular  
to assess whether revenue received in advance is correctly 
recognised and accounted for and the overall completeness

concluded that the timing of recognition continues to be in  
line with IFRS requirements and that all material balances  
were captured. The external auditor performed detailed audit 
procedures on revenue recognition, including auditing a sample  
of admissions, reconciling these back to the revenues recorded 
and performing cut-off testing around the year end to ensure 
revenue is recognised in the period to which it relates,

Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 54 Exceptional items
The Committee noted that the Group had significant exceptional 
items in the financial year, arising from the cancellation of a 
business change project on which significant non-recurring costs 
had been incurred and also one-off business restructuring costs. 
In addition, the treatment as an exceptional item of the asset 
impairment charge arising from the review of fixed assets was 
noted. The Committee therefore considered that such items 
should be an area of particular scrutiny. The audit plan agreed 
reviewed the one-off items of expense and income to ensure  
they were appropriately classified and were properly considered 
non-recurring and exceptional in nature and the treatment of the 
asset impairment charge. After consideration of the results of this 
review, the Committee was satisfied that any material items of 
non-recurring expense or income were properly classified and 
that the asset impairment charge should appear separately on 
the face of the income statement. Details of these exceptional 
items are disclosed in note 5 on pages 98 and 99. 
Recovery of trade receivables
Given the nature of the Group’s customers, debts are often 
overdue beyond the contractual payment date and the Group  
has a significant level of aged debt. The Committee therefore 
considered the appropriateness of the Group’s policy for 
provision for debts greater than 120 days and the level of risk  
that exists around the recoverability of overdue debts. In the  
light of this review it was agreed to change the policy and 
provision for all debts more than 180 days old and the audit  
plan agreed with the external auditors therefore placed 
emphasis on a detailed review of aged receivables, and 
included an assessment of recoverability from a sample of 
receivables. Following this review, the Committee was satisfied  
that adequate provisions were being made for any potentially 
irrecoverable debtor balances.
Acquisitions
The Group made a number of acquisitions during the year, 
including the acquisition of By the Bridge Holdings Limited and  
its subsidiaries, the acquisition of Interact Care Limited and the 
business and assets of Potterspury Lodge School and Spring  
Hill School. The Committee reviewed the significant judgments 
required in respect of the purchase price allocation process, 
which includes the fair valuation of the assets and liabilities 
acquired, including separately identifying and valuing acquired 
intangible assets to ensure that acquisitions are accounted  
for appropriately in accordance with IFRS 3 (Business 
Combinations). The proper treatment of acquisitions was  
also a focus of review by the external auditor, who reviewed  
the assumptions underpinning the fair value of assets and 
liabilities and the intangible asset valuation. After consideration  
of these matters, the Committee was satisfied that acquisitions 
made during the year had been properly accounted for in the 
financial statements.
Completeness of liabilities
Following the issues experienced by the Group in managing  
its cost base, the auditors conducted an additional review of 
expense and in particular accruals to ensure the completeness 
of the liabilities recorded in the balance sheet. Following this 
review, it was considered that the balance sheet as at 31 
December 2015 properly recorded or made appropriate  
accruals for all known liabilities of the Group.
Other matters
The Group entered into an interest rate swap in relation to a 
portion of the Group’s bank debt in order to minimise volatility  
in the income statement and the Committee reviewed the 
accounting treatment applied in relation to this transaction,  
which was also an area of review by the external auditor.
Review of the 2015 Annual Report
At the request of the Board, the Committee was asked to  
consider whether the 2015 Annual Report was fair, balanced  
and capable of being understood by shareholders. In order  
to arrive at a position where the Committee was satisfied with  
the overall fairness, balance and clarity of the Annual Report,  
a comprehensive review process was followed.
During the course of the Committee’s review, the following 
questions were considered for debate:
• Fairness and balance: Is the Annual Report open and honest? 
Does it report on weaknesses, difficulties and challenges as well 
as successes? Is there consistency between different sections  
of the Annual Report, including between the narrative and the 
financial statements? Does the Annual Report explain our key 
performance indicators (KPIs) and their linkage to strategy?
• Understandable: Does the Annual Report contain simple 
explanations of business models, strategies and accounting 
policies, using precise and clear language? Is the Annual Report 
easy to read; for example, is the narrative broken up by quotes, 
tables, case studies and other graphics? Does the Annual 
Report have a consistent tone across all sections and provide 
clear signposting to where additional information can be found? 
After careful review, the Committee was satisfied that, taken as a 
whole, the Annual Report was fair, balanced and capable of being 
understood by shareholders, and advised the Board accordingly.

Governance The Company’s internal control is based on assessment of risk 
and a framework of control procedures to manage risks and  
to monitor compliance with procedures. The procedures for 
accountability and control are split between operational and 
financial matters. Financial controls are reviewed and their 
effectiveness assessed by the Committee and tested by work 
undertaken by the internal auditors. In particular, given the cost 
control issues that impacted the Company’s performance in the 
year, the internal auditors were commissioned at the end of the 
year to undertake a detailed review of key balance sheet controls.
The Group’s activities expose it to significant operational risks, 
principally medical, clinical and health & safety risks. As described 
on pages 26 to 29, the Group has in place risk management 
systems and protocols in relation to the operational risks facing 
the Group. Cambian’s governance protocols are aimed at ensuring 
consistently high quality care to mitigate these risks. These protocols 
operate at three levels:
• at individual site level through monthly meetings;
• at the executive level through weekly and monthly meetings  
of the executive management committee; and
• at a corporate level through quarterly meetings of Cambian’s 
Governance Committee, which reviews the Group’s 
performance in these areas.
In addition, the Group operates a Quality Management System 
that has gained BS EN ISO 9001: 2008 certification, including 
aspects specific to education, social care for people with autism 
and complex needs, healthcare, residential and day services. 
Through these frameworks, the Group monitors its quality 
performance on a continuing basis and aims to implement 
improvements and changes when determined to be appropriate. 
In the highly regulated environment in which the Company operates, 
procedures are codified in detailed operating procedures and policies 
and these are reinforced by training programmes. These are 
designed to ensure compliance not only with the regulatory 
requirements but also with general principles of integrity and the 
Group’s philosophy that everyone can achieve their personal best.
The Committee has during the year identified and evaluated the 
key risks and has ensured that controls and procedures are in 
place to manage these risks and to improve these processes 
where weaknesses are identified. 
Internal audit
The internal audit function plays an important role in assessing 
the effectiveness of internal controls by a programme of reviews 
based on a continuous assessment of the strategic risk register.  
It is important that the internal audit function is appropriately 
resourced with the skills and experience relevant to the operations 
of the Group, and is supported by specialist resources where 
required. Given the importance of the internal audit function and 
the resources required and the fact that at the start of the financial 
year the Company had only recently completed its IPO, the Board 
determined to appoint an external firm as internal auditor 
responsible for reviewing, reporting and monitoring improvements 
in internal control performance across its operations. Following  
a review process, involving the Chair of the Committee and  
the Group’s Chief Finance Officer, it was agreed to appoint 
PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP (“PwC”) to carry-out the function  
of internal audit for the Group. 
Following their appointment, PwC worked with the Company to 
review the principal strategic risks facing the Group, following 
which it agreed an initial programme of work with the Committee 
that was designed to provide assurance in the key areas of risk to 
the business, as well as in the areas of core financial and internal 
control, and where there are regulatory or legal requirements.  
A key focus of internal audit activity in 2015 has been on providing 
assurance on key financial control activities. 
The system of internal controls and audit is designed to ensure 
legal and regulatory compliance and manage, rather than 
eliminate, the risk of failure to achieve business objectives.  
It can therefore only provide reasonable and not absolute 
assurance against material misstatement or loss. 
Internal control & risk management
The Company has in place internal controls in relation to the 
Company’s financial reporting process and the Group’s process  
for preparation of consolidated accounts. These systems include 
policies and procedures that: pertain to the maintenance of 
records that, in reasonable detail, accurately and fairly reflect 
transactions and dispositions of assets; provide reasonable 
assurance that transactions are recorded as necessary to  
permit the preparation of financial statements in accordance  
with International Financial Reporting Standards (‘IFRS’); require 
representatives of the businesses to certify that their reported 
information gives a true and fair view of the state of affairs of  
the business and its results for the period; and review and 
reconcile reported data. The Committee is responsible for 
monitoring these internal control and risk management systems. 
Audit & Risk Committee report
continued
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 56 External audit
The Committee manages the relationship with the external  
auditor (currently, Deloitte LLP (“Deloitte”)) on behalf of the Board. 
This includes assessing the independence of the external auditor, 
conducting annual evaluations of the external auditor and 
providing final recommendations to the Board on their reappointment, 
remuneration and the level of non-audit fees paid to the auditors.
Auditor’s independence
The Board undertakes a formal assessment of the auditor’s 
independence each year, which includes:
• A review of non-audit related services provided to the  
Company and related fees;
• Discussion with the auditor of a written report detailing all 
relationships with the Company and any other parties which 
could affect independence or the perception of independence;
• A review of the auditor’s own procedures for ensuring 
independence of the audit firm and partners and staff involved 
in the audit, including the rotation of the audit partner;
• Obtaining written confirmation from the auditors that they  
are independent; and
• A review of fees paid to the auditors in respect of audit and 
non-audit services.
Non-audit work undertaken
Cambian follows a pre-approval policy for the provision of 
non-audit services by the external auditor. Other accounting  
firms were used for larger, non-audit services, including taxation 
and consultancy advice. Details of services provided by the auditor 
and its associates are included in note 6 on page 99. The focus  
of the policy is to ensure that the independence of the external 
auditor is not compromised and, where possible and appropriate, 
other accounting firms are used. During 2015, the external auditor 
conducted engagements for the provision of non-audit services, 
relating to due diligence in relation to the acquisition of By the 
Bridge Limited, a review of pension payments and a capital 
allowances review totalling £178,000, approximately 29%  
of the audit fee.
The Committee has monitored the development of EU legislation 
in respect of auditors and audit reporting, and in particular the 
provisions of EU Regulation No.537/2014 which will introduce  
(from 2020) a cap on fees for certain non-audit services at 70%  
of the external audit fee, as well as a prohibition on the provision 
of certain non-audit services by the incumbent external auditor. 
The Committee will ensure that the Group will comply with these 
provisions and that the policy on non-audit services will be 
reviewed in line with the Regulation. 
Deloitte was selected to undertake these tasks due to its familiarity 
with the Cambian business and the industry. In order to maintain 
independence and objectivity, Deloitte undertook its standard 
independence procedures in relation to those engagements. 
Auditor’s effectiveness
Deloitte LLP was re-appointed as the auditor at the Annual General 
Meeting in April 2015. The firm was appointed auditor when the 
Company was incorporated as it had acted as auditor to all of  
the companies that were brought together to form the Group 
immediately prior to the initial public offer in April 2014 and so had 
extensive knowledge of the business. Continuity and consistency  
of audit quality are important and the Committee has no current 
intention to initiate an audit re-tendering process. Going forward, 
the Committee will consider a formal tender process in accordance 
with the provisions of the Code. The Committee will comply with the 
Competition & Markets Authority order relating to the statutory audit 
market for FTSE 350 companies, as applicable.
The Committee has adopted a formal framework for the review 
and assess the effectiveness of the external audit process and 
audit quality, which includes the following aspects:
• Assessment of the engagement partner, other partners and 
members of the audit team;
• Audit approach and scope, including clarification of  
audit risk areas;
• Execution of the audit;
• Interaction with management;
• Communication with and support to the Audit Committee; 
• Insights, management letter points and reporting; and
• Independence, objectivity and scepticism.
The Committee assesses the effectiveness of the management  
of the external audit process by considering timely identification 
and resolution of areas of accounting judgment, the quality and 
timeliness of papers reporting to the Committee on these matters 
and the quality of any other documents provided to the Committee 
during the external audit process.
Cambian Group plc
Annual Report and Accounts 2015 57
Governance Nomination Committee report
The Nomination Committee comprises Christopher Kemball 
(Chairman), and all of the independent non-executive directors  
in office at the date of this report. Alfred Foglio is entitled to  
attend meetings of the Committee as an observer. Details of the 
Chairman’s other significant commitments are set out on page 44.
 
The Nomination Committee meets at least once a year and on  
an as needed basis and members’ attendance is set out in the 
table opposite. 
The Nomination Committee reviews the structure, size and 
composition of the Board and its committees and makes 
recommendations with regard to any changes considered 
necessary in the identification and nomination of new directors,  
the reappointment of existing directors and appointment of 
members to the Board’s committees. It also assesses the roles  
of the existing directors in office to ensure that there continues to  
be a balanced Board in terms of skills, knowledge, experience and 
diversity. The Nomination Committee reviews the senior leadership 
needs of the Group to enable it to compete effectively in the 
marketplace. The Nomination Committee also advises the Board  
on succession planning for executive director appointments 
although the Board itself is responsible for succession generally.
The Nomination Committee seeks to ensure that all Board 
appointments are made on merit and measured against objective 
criteria and with due regard for the benefits of diversity on the 
Board. The Board is committed to ensuring a broad mix of gender, 
age, nationality, experience and skills throughout the business. The 
composition of the Board itself is based on a range and balance of 
skills, knowledge, experience and merit and remains appropriate 
for a business of its size. The Nomination Committee ensures that 
diversity is an important consideration and part of the selective 
criteria used to assess candidates to achieve a balanced Board.
The Nomination Committee met twice in 2015. The first meeting 
considered the appointment of an Independent Non-executive  
Director from a list of candidates drawn up following an 
independent recruitment process run by Egon Zehnder.  
This meeting resulted in the recommendation to the Board  
to appoint Dr Graham Rich.
The other meeting during the year focused on consideration of 
results of the independent evaluation of the performance of the 
Board conducted by Lintstock and on the continued applicability  
of the Committee’s terms of reference, which were considered  
to continue to be appropriate for the Company.

Dear Shareholder
I am pleased to present our remuneration report for the financial 
year ended 31st December 2015.
At the 2015 Annual General Meeting, the shareholders voted  
by a majority of 85% of the votes cast to approve the directors’ 
remuneration policy as set out in the directors’ remuneration report 
contained in the Cambian 2014 Annual Report and Accounts.
That policy was an evolution of the remuneration framework 
adopted at the Company’s IPO in 2014, involving some 
amendments to ensure good corporate governance and to  
ensure the policy remained appropriate, given the transition  
from a private company to a listed company. These changes 
included increasing the deferral period from options granted 
under the Cambian Group Annual Share Option Plan (“AOP”)  
to a period of three years, introducing malus and clawback 
provisions and a shareholding requirement for executive  
directors and making minor changes to basic salary and  
pension provision to better reflect the market. 
As part of the shareholder consultation process we undertook  
last year, I explained to shareholders that the remuneration policy 
put forward reflected transitional arrangements as we evolved 
into a listed entity. As planned, the Committee and I have worked 
extensively during 2015 to review the policy and create a structure 
that is more appropriate for both our executives in supporting our 
business strategy and which genuinely reflects the experience of 
our shareholders.
As a result of this review, the Committee is now putting forward  
a revised policy, which reflects the shareholder feedback we 
received last year, for shareholders to approve at the Cambian 
2016 Annual General Meeting (“2016 AGM”). 
New proposed directors’ remuneration policy
Key changes to the proposed policy are summarised below:
• Reduction of the annual bonus opportunity for the Chief 
Executive Officer (CEO) to a maximum of 150% of base salary, 
payable in cash, though the Committee has a discretion for  
part to be deferred into options under the AOP. The annual 
bonus opportunity of the Chief Financial Officer has remained 
unchanged. The annual bonus will be determined by 
performance against a mix of financial and operational targets 
and at least half the bonus will be dependent on achievement  
of the financial target, with the requirement for a threshold 
achievement against the financial target being necessary 
before any payment can be made under the plan, whether  
or not the other targets have been met. For 2016, 40% of the 
maximum bonus will be payable for on-target performance;
The Board has delegated formation of its 
policy for the remuneration of the directors 
and senior management to the Remuneration 
Committee (the “Committee”), which also has 
oversight over the Group’s share plans.

Annual Report and Accounts 2015 60 At a glance
Introduction
In this section, we summarise the purpose of our proposed remuneration policy, its linkage to our corporate strategic objectives and  
we highlight the performance and remuneration outcomes for the 2015 financial year. More detail can be found in the annual report  
on remuneration of which this section forms a part.
Our principles of remuneration
The Company’s remuneration strategy is to provide remuneration packages that:
• Attract, motivate and retain high performing employees;
• Encourage and support a strong care and service culture;
• Reward the achievement of the overall business objectives of the Company;
• Align employees’ interests with those of shareholders; and
• Are consistent with the Company’s risk policies and systems.
Consistent with this remuneration strategy, the Committee has agreed a remuneration package for the management team, whereby:
• Performance-related pay will form a significant part of remuneration packages; 
• There will be an appropriate balance between short and longer-term performance targets linked to delivery of the Group’s objectives; and
• In the event of a serious failure in the quality of care provided by the Group, or a failure to achieve threshold financial performance, 
this would act as an override to prevent payment of any bonus that might otherwise be payable in respect of that year.

is given to remuneration committees.
